<h3><a name="page-1131822">CB03_0003</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>3</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn <date when='1873-03-17'>Mar. 17, 1873</date></p>
<p>[?] Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I <u>think</u> <a href='/pages/subjects/104089' title='Frost, Samuel T.'>Mr. <!--S. T.-->Frost</a> can purchase an ad<span class='line-break'></span>dition of 150 sq. ft. as per enclosed sketch,<span class='line-break'> </span>Making his whole lot 450 ft. when done,<span class='line-break'> </span>being 24 ft deep by 18 ft [?]</p>
<p>Cost ---<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>150 ft of land @ $1.00</th> <th>$150.00<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Deed</td> <td>$2.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>[Total]</td> <td>$152.00</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> 			              <span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>, Supt.</p>
<p>P.S. Before committing [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] to [?] curbing<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp;c - Mr. Frost should complete<span class='line-break'> </span>the [illegible] get his certif<span class='line-break'></span>cate [illegible]</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W.F.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</a><span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131823">
<h3><a name="page-1131823">CB03_0004</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p> 4</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn Cemetery.<span class='line-break'> </span>Office of Superintendant,<span class='line-break'> </span>Mt. Auburn, <date when='1873-03-19'>March 19. 1873 </date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/60684' title='Stone, James F.'>Mr. Stone</a>,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>A party in search of a <span class='line-break'> </span>small lot has made enquiry in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>the space in rear of your <a href='/pages/subjects/104092' title='Lot 3769'>lot #3769</a>.</p>
<p>By the Bye-laws [sic] of the Corporation,<span class='line-break'> </span>you have the right to take the land at<span class='line-break'> </span>1/3 the price, at which it would be sold as<span class='line-break'> </span>a separate lot, on condition of making no<span class='line-break'> </span>interments therein<span class='line-break'> </span>holding it as a <ins>passage-way</ins>.</p>
<p>Its form is rectangular,<span class='line-break'> </span>15 ft. x 6 = 90 sq. ft.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>90 ft. @ .33 Â¢ per ft. =</th> <th>$30.00<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Deed</td> <td><ins> 2.00 </ins>  </td> </tr> <tr><td>[Total]</td> <td>$32.00</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>[Image: diagram of <a href='/pages/subjects/104092' title='Lot 3769'>Lot 3769</a> on <a href='/pages/subjects/61161' title='Cuphea Path'>Cuphea Path</a> and <a href='/pages/subjects/58081' title='Halcyon Avenue'>Halcyon Avenue</a>. 15ft at top of image, 7ft at right; inside rectangle is 6 ft on both top left and right side,  90 sq ft. top center. Also inside are two lines a 1/4 of the way down with illegible text and the number 3769 underneath the bottom line. on either end of the two lines are darkened circles, the right hand one has 6ft under it; 2 dark circles are at each bottom corner of the rectangle. a path drawing is alongside the rectangle named [Cuphea Path]; underneath [Halcyon Ave.]</p>
<p>Please inform me at your<span class='line-break'> </span>earliest convenience,<span class='line-break'> </span>whether you wish to do anything<span class='line-break'> </span>in regard to the matter</p>
<p>Respectfully yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131824">
<h3><a name="page-1131824">CB03_0005</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent's Office<span class='line-break'> </span>(P.O.) Mt. Auburn, Mass.<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-03-25'>Mar. 25, 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/104096' title='Litchfield, R.'>R. Litchfield Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Enclosed please find<span class='line-break'> </span>your bill of <date when='1869-11-13'>Nov. 13, [18]69</date>.</p>
<p>As the bill was incurred some<span class='line-break'> </span>time before, I took charge here and ^<sup>as</sup> I know<span class='line-break'> </span>nothing about it, it would be better to send<span class='line-break'> </span>it direct to the President of the Corporation.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>Mr. John T. Bradlee</a><span class='line-break'> </span>134 State St.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a></p>
<p>together with a statement of the circumstances.</p>
<p>Yours Respectfully,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131825">
<h3><a name="page-1131825">CB03_0006</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery.<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent's Office<span class='line-break'> </span>(P.O.) Mt Auburn, Mass<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-03-25'>March 25, 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/104097' title='Brewer, Mr.'>Mr. Brewer</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In your letter of <date when='1873-03-21'>21<sup>st</sup></date> inst, recd<span class='line-break'> </span>you asked to have made and set "a granite foun<span class='line-break'></span>"dation" for a tablet, on your lot.</p>
<p>The regular <ins>underground</ins> foundation<span class='line-break'> </span>has been ordered ^ <sup>by me;</sup> but we did not quite under<span class='line-break'></span>stand whether you wished us to furnish the<span class='line-break'> </span>ground or not. This "base" is usually included <span class='line-break'> </span>in the contract of the man who furnishes the<span class='line-break'> </span>tablet or monument, but if you wish us to fur<span class='line-break'></span>nish it we will do so.</p>
<p>Please inform as at your earliest con<span class='line-break'></span>venience in regard to the matter, and oblige</p>
<p>Yours Respectfully,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131826">
<h3><a name="page-1131826">CB03_0007</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>7</p>
<p><date when='1873-03-25'>March 25 /[18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee</a> Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Rest - Dear Sir</p>
<p>I enclose<span class='line-break'> </span>herewith a schedule of all the<span class='line-break'> </span>new worth naming who were<span class='line-break'> </span>employed at any time during<span class='line-break'> </span>1872, with their rates of<span class='line-break'> </span>pay; thinking that you<span class='line-break'> </span>might find it useful in<span class='line-break'> </span>hiring by and by for 1873.</p>
<p>Yours very truly,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131827">
<h3><a name="page-1131827">CB03_0008</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>8</p>
<p><date when='1873-03-25'>March 25 /[18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/95125' title='Snow, Samuel T.'>Sam<sup>l</sup> T. Snow</a>. Esq.,<span class='line-break'> </span>Chair<sup>n</sup> Comm on Lots</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>About four days ago<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Mr. Jonathan Mann</a> came to me as<span class='line-break'> </span>agent for <a href='/pages/subjects/104105' title='Buchnam, G. C., Mr.'>Mr G.C. Buchnam</a>, prop<sup>r</sup>,<span class='line-break'> </span>of <a href='/pages/subjects/104106' title='Lot 4215'>lot. 4215</a><a href='/pages/subjects/104107' title='Lot 4216'> - <!--Lot 42-->16,</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/59983' title='Hazel Dell'>Hazel Dell</a>, to<span class='line-break'> </span>see on what terms we would do<span class='line-break'> </span>the labor &amp; finish the staple materials<span class='line-break'> </span>for a tomb he is preparing to build<span class='line-break'> </span>there.</p>
<p>I asked him to put<span class='line-break'> </span>his ideas in writing, but as time<span class='line-break'> </span>pressed, I wrote them down &amp; he<span class='line-break'> </span>signed the letter which I enclose.</p>
<p>I also enclose<span class='line-break'> </span>a draft of a letter about such.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131828">
<h3><a name="page-1131828">CB03_0009</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>9</p>
<p>as I should have written in similar<span class='line-break'> </span>cases; but under the circum<span class='line-break'></span>stances I thought it right to<span class='line-break'> </span>submit the matter for your<span class='line-break'> </span>action before making any con<span class='line-break'></span>tract with him.</p>
<p>The prices I have<span class='line-break'> </span>named to him are our regular<span class='line-break'> </span>rates, as near as possible, for<span class='line-break'> </span>jobbers or "the trade" <del> about 10%<span class='line-break'> </span>lower or</del> from 5 to 10 per cent<span class='line-break'> </span>lower on labor, gravel, loam, manure<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; sods, than our regular rates to<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors, but on brick,<span class='line-break'> </span>lime &amp; cement no lower.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Mr. Mann</a> would<span class='line-break'> </span>like an answer this week, <span class='line-break'> </span>as he has to make arrange<span class='line-break'></span>ments of <u>some kind</u> pretty soon<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131829">
<h3><a name="page-1131829">CB03_0010</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>10</p>
<p>(3)<span class='line-break'> </span>to commence with the open<span class='line-break'></span>ing of spring.</p>
<p>We have another<span class='line-break'> </span>tomb engaged to build on the<span class='line-break'> </span><u>very next lot</u> to <a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>Mr. Buck<span class='line-break'></span>nam's</a> as early as spring<span class='line-break'> </span>opens; - which is what<span class='line-break'> </span>I refer to by "one half of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/105021' title='Day, John M.'>J. M. Day's</a>" (our head mason's) time;<span class='line-break'> </span>meaning that he should "boss"<span class='line-break'> </span>both gangs at once which I<span class='line-break'> </span>think he could do.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>Mr. Bucknam's</a> tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>is generally similar to the other<span class='line-break'> </span>tombs in <a href='/pages/subjects/59983' title='Hazel Dell'>Hazel Dell</a>, &amp; not</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131830">
<h3><a name="page-1131830">CB03_0011</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>11</p>
<p>(4)</p>
<p>larger; it is to have a<span class='line-break'> </span>^<sup>granite front sand</sup> stone arched roof in part.</p>
<p>The other tomb we<span class='line-break'> </span>are to build is exactly<span class='line-break'> </span>like the other tomb there;<span class='line-break'> </span>granite front &amp; brick arched roof.</p>
<p>Yours Truly,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>P.S. I enclose <a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Mr<span class='line-break'> </span>Mann's</a> plan of the granite front,<span class='line-break'> </span>which please return &amp; oblige</p>
<p>Yours truly, <a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W.F.<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</a></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131831">
<h3><a name="page-1131831">CB03_0012</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>12</p>
<p>[Notation: Rough copy; Whole page Cancelled]</p>
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery,<span class='line-break'> </span>Superintendent's Office<span class='line-break'> </span>(P.O.) Mt. Auburn</p>
<p><date when='1873-03-25'>Mar 25 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Jonathan Mann Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In reply to your letter <span class='line-break'> </span>of 21st inst, asking on what terms the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corp<sup>n</sup> will undertake to build a tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>for <a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>Mr. J. C. Bucknam</a>, on his <a href='/pages/subjects/104106' title='Lot 4215'>lots 4215</a> &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/104107' title='Lot 4216'><!--42-->16</a><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/59983' title='Hazel Dell'>Hazel Dell</a>, (the stone &amp;c for which are now<span class='line-break'> </span>on the ground,) I would reply, that we<span class='line-break'> </span>will be prepared to build the tomb by the<span class='line-break'> </span>day; charging $3.00 per day each, for each<span class='line-break'> </span>man of the mason's gang of 4 men, or for the<span class='line-break'> </span>derrick; and $2.50 per day each for each man<span class='line-break'> </span>of the grading gang; We would use our best<span class='line-break'> </span>masons, or as good as we have, but could<span class='line-break'> </span>only give one half of <a href='/pages/subjects/105021' title='Day, John M.'>John M. Day's</a> time;<span class='line-break'> </span>and if necessary to hire bricklayers from<span class='line-break'> </span>outside, would charge you 10 per cent ad<span class='line-break'></span>vance on their cost to us.</p>
<p>We would furnish brick, lime and<span class='line-break'> </span>cement at the following profit on their cost<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>to us - Brick</th> <th>15 per ct.<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Cement</td> <td>10 [per ct]</td> </tr> <tr><td>Lime</td> <td>10 [per ct]</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> (over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131832">
<h3><a name="page-1131832">CB03_0013</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>13</p>
<p>[Notation: rough copy; whole page cancelled]</p>
<p>(the cost of hauling from our storehouses<span class='line-break'> </span>to be charged in addition, if necessary to haul<span class='line-break'> </span>them, but the brick and cement could un<span class='line-break'></span>doubtedly be delivered by the contractors on<span class='line-break'> </span>the spot.)</p>
<p>We would furnish<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Gravel at</th> <th>.50Â¢ per load<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Loam  [at]</td> <td>$1.00 [per load]</td> </tr> <tr><td>Manure</td> <td>3.00 [per load]</td> </tr> <tr><td>Sand (for mortar)</td> <td>2.00 [per load]</td> </tr> <tr><td>Sods -</td> <td>63 3/4Â¢ per ft.</td> </tr> <tr><td>Galvanized clamps</td> <td>.25Â¢ each</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> any other clamps or small extras @<span class='line-break'> </span>10 per ct. advance on cost to us.</p>
<p>Foundation or other stone @ 15%<span class='line-break'> </span>advance on cost, besides cartage of needed</p>
<p>Truly Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'><!--C.W.F.-->Superintendent</a></p>

<div id="page-1131833">
<h3><a name="page-1131833">CB03_0014</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>14</p>
<p>Mount Auburn Cemetery,<span class='line-break'> </span>Office of Supt,</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-03-31'>M[ar]ch 31, 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Jona. Mann, Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In reply to your<span class='line-break'> </span>letter of<date when='1873-03-21'> 21<sup>st</sup> inst.</date> asking on what terms<span class='line-break'> </span>the Corp. will undertake to build a tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>for <a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>Mr. J.C. Bucknam</a> on his [Lot 4215|[lots 4215]]<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/104107' title='Lot 4216'>&amp; 4216</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/59983' title='Hazel Dell'>Hazel Dell</a> (the stone &amp;c for which<span class='line-break'> </span>are now on the ground,) I would reply,<span class='line-break'> </span>that we will be prepared to build the tomb<span class='line-break'> </span><u>by the day</u>; charging $3.00 per day each<span class='line-break'> </span>for each man of the mason's gang of 4 men, or<span class='line-break'> </span>for the derrick; and $2.50 per day each, for<span class='line-break'> </span>each man of the grading gang;</p>
<p>We would use our best<span class='line-break'> </span>masons or as good as we have, but could<span class='line-break'> </span>give only one half of <a href='/pages/subjects/105021' title='Day, John M.'>John M Day's</a> time;<span class='line-break'> </span>and if neessary to hire bricklayers from<span class='line-break'> </span>outside would charge you 10 per cent advance<span class='line-break'> </span>on their cost to us.</p>
<p>We would furnish brick, foundation<span class='line-break'></span>stone, lime and cement at 10 per cent advance</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131834">
<h3><a name="page-1131834">CB03_0015</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>15</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>on their cost to us delivered on the spot.<span class='line-break'> </span>(In this way the cost of hauling from our storehouses<span class='line-break'> </span>will be charged in addition, if necessary to<span class='line-break'> </span>haul them; but the brick and cement could<span class='line-break'> </span>undoubtedly be del'd by the contractors on<span class='line-break'> </span>the spot.)</p>
<p>We would furnish <u>sand</u> (for mortar)<span class='line-break'> </span>at $2.00 per load, Galvanized clamps any<span class='line-break'> </span>other clamps or small extras at our usual<span class='line-break'> </span>rate.</p>
<p>Payments for work done or materials<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered to be made monthly</p>
<p>(The above relates to the^<sup>excavating &amp;</sup> masonry of<span class='line-break'> </span>the <u>tomb</u> solely.</p>
<p>The grading &amp; sodding of the<span class='line-break'> </span><u>lots</u>, I think had better be made a separate<span class='line-break'> </span>proposition.</p>
<p>Truly Yours,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131835">
<h3><a name="page-1131835">CB03_0016</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>16</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>Office of Supt.</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-04-05'>April 5 [18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/105044' title='Stone, James M.'>Jas. M. Stone Esq</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I enclose herewith the<span class='line-break'> </span>Certificate of the space in the rear<span class='line-break'> </span>of your lot, and in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>grading the lot to correspond with<span class='line-break'> </span>others on the Avenue, would say<span class='line-break'> </span>that I think it would be a<span class='line-break'> </span>decided improvement. I think the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost would be about $35.00 if the <span class='line-break'> </span>same sods were used again; or<span class='line-break'> </span>about $60.00, if entirely new sods<span class='line-break'> </span>were furnished.</p>
<p>Respectfully Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131836">
<h3><a name="page-1131836">CB03_0017</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>17</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-05'>April 5 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/105048' title='Messrs. Philbrick &amp; Sargent'>Messrs. Philbrick &amp; Sargent</a>,</p>
<p>Gents,</p>
<p>In reply to your letter of<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-03-18'>Mar. 18<sup>th</sup></date> would say, the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>is prepared to set the curb you spoke of,<span class='line-break'> </span>on <a href='/pages/subjects/72189' title='Lot 579'>lot #579</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/58080' title='Maple Avenue'>Maple Av.</a> The enclosed sketch<span class='line-break'> </span>gives the difference in hight [sic] of the corners<span class='line-break'> </span>of the lot also the hight [sic] of the middle of<span class='line-break'> </span>front of lot above gutter. The measurements<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Deed are expected to agree with the<span class='line-break'> </span>inside measurements of the curb.</p>
<p>The Corp terms for setting curb are as<span class='line-break'> </span>follows</p>
<p>Labor - $3.00 per day for each man's time<span class='line-break'> </span>Foundation stone at 10 per ct. advance<span class='line-break'> </span>on the cost to us delivered on the spot.<span class='line-break'> </span>Gal. Clamps and other small extras at our<span class='line-break'> </span>usual rates.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W.Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>[Note: Sketch on  P.18. Letter Book.]</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131847">
<h3><a name="page-1131847">CB03_0029</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>29</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/105144' title='Coolidge, Mr.'>Mr. Coolidge</a> had a quantity of blank<span class='line-break'> </span>paper stored at the office.</p>
<p>It is difficult to estimate cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>revising the general map of the Cem.<span class='line-break'> </span>without a completed copy to compare<span class='line-break'> </span>and see what is to be done.</p>
<p>The above is from <a href='/pages/subjects/105117' title='Meisel, Augustus'>Mr Meisel</a>:</p>
<p>The cost of constantly revising maps<span class='line-break'> </span>by hand for the use of all the Committees,<span class='line-break'> </span>offices, and principal employees of the <span class='line-break'> </span>Cemetery is very considerable.</p>
<p>I have often thought the amt. expended<span class='line-break'> </span>in clerk hire in this direction, would pay<span class='line-break'> </span>for correcting the stone.</p>
<p>Respectfully Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>30</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-08'>April 8 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee Esq Pres't.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I wish to call to your<span class='line-break'> </span>notice, the piece of ground or "Park" so called<span class='line-break'> </span>situated between <a href='/pages/subjects/58791' title='Central Avenue'>Central<!--Ave--></a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/58079' title='Garden Avenue'>Garden<!--Ave--></a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/58084' title='Yew Avenue'>Yew<!--Ave--></a> and<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/72315' title='Fountain Avenue'>Fountain Aves</a>, on the left of <a href='/pages/subjects/57664' title='Entrance Gateway'>the main Gate</a>.</p>
<p>Last year a large quantity of <span class='line-break'> </span>manure was carted on to it, alas con<span class='line-break'></span>siderable loam, with a view to plowing<span class='line-break'> </span>in this spring,</p>
<p>The material is scattered over the<span class='line-break'> </span>ground in heaps, and I respectfully recom<span class='line-break'></span>mend that as soon as the weather is favorable.<span class='line-break'> </span>the heaps should be spread and the whole<span class='line-break'> </span>plowed over.</p>
<p>Yours Truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a> Supt.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131850">
<h3><a name="page-1131850">CB03_0032</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>32</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-08'>8<sup>th</sup> April 1873</date></p>
<p>Mess<sup>rs</sup> <a href='/pages/subjects/105158' title='P. O&apos;Brian &amp; Co.'>P. O'Brien &amp; Co</a></p>
<p>Gentlemen,</p>
<p>My attention has been called to<span class='line-break'> </span>the fact that the By-laws (page 28 Article XII) and<span class='line-break'> </span>uniform in their provisions which require that <u>all<span class='line-break'> </span>persons</u> who perform work for Proprietors shall hand<span class='line-break'> </span>a permit from each Proprietor who so employs him.</p>
<p>I think it is the wish of our Trustees that<span class='line-break'> </span>this privision shall be strictly carried out, and<span class='line-break'> </span>would notify you now that I think a permit will<span class='line-break'> </span>be required of you for each lot for which you may have<span class='line-break'> </span>an order for care or other work for this coming season.</p>
<p>Several of the large Stone - dealers have<span class='line-break'> </span>procured a <u>general permit</u> on giving the proper bonds;<span class='line-break'> </span>and it is possible that some such arrangement will<span class='line-break'> </span>be practicable in your case, accompanied with a return<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131851">
<h3><a name="page-1131851">CB03_0033</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>33</p>
<p>from you of a list of orders which you may <span class='line-break'> </span>receive.</p>
<p>If you desire such, I would recommend<span class='line-break'> </span>that application be made for it to the Trustees,<span class='line-break'> </span>without delay, to avoid embarrassment<span class='line-break'> </span>to yourself.</p>
<p>Very truly yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W.Folsom</a>, Sup't</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131852">
<h3><a name="page-1131852">CB03_0034</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>34</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-08'>8<sup>th</sup> April 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/74568' title='Fox, Joseph'>Joseph Fox</a> Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>My attention has been called to the<span class='line-break'> </span>fact that the By-laws (page 28 Article XII.) are <u>uniform</u><span class='line-break'> </span>in their provisions which require that <u>all persons</u> who<span class='line-break'> </span>perform work for Proprietors shall have a <u>permit</u> from<span class='line-break'> </span>Proprietor who so employs him.</p>
<p>I think it is the wish of our Trustees that<span class='line-break'> </span>provision shall be strictly carried out, and would notify<span class='line-break'> </span>now that I think a permit will be required of you for each<span class='line-break'> </span>lot for which you may have an order for care or other work<span class='line-break'> </span>for the coming season.</p>
<p>Several of the large stone-dealers have procured<span class='line-break'> </span>a <u>general permit</u> on giving the proper bonds; and it is<span class='line-break'> </span>possible that some such arrangement will be practicable<span class='line-break'> </span>in your case, accompanied with a return from you of a <span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131853">
<h3><a name="page-1131853">CB03_0035</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>35</p>
<p>list of orders which you may receive.</p>
<p>If you desire such, I would recommend that<span class='line-break'> </span>application be made for it to the Trustees without delay,<span class='line-break'> </span>to avoid embarrassment to yourself.</p>
<p>Very truly yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>, Sup't</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131854">
<h3><a name="page-1131854">CB03_0036</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>36</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-09'>Apr. 9 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee</a>, Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>The supply of<span class='line-break'> </span><u>Guides</u> which have hitherto been kept<span class='line-break'> </span>on sale by the <a href='/pages/subjects/105198' title='Spears, George G.'><!--Spears-->Gate Keeper</a> is exhausted.</p>
<p>I think it very desireable<span class='line-break'> </span>to Mt. Auburn, that they should be<span class='line-break'> </span>kept on sale.</p>
<p>Accordingly I requested<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/105156' title='Stafford, Mr.'>Mr. Safford</a> to make enquiries as to<span class='line-break'> </span>the prospect of obtaining more and<span class='line-break'> </span>his letter and that of the owners of<span class='line-break'> </span>the "Guide" are enclosed.</p>
<p>I also enclose a copy of<span class='line-break'> </span>the latest "Guide" and four (4) old ones</p>
<p>Respectfully Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25006734' title='K., E. T. Staff'>Per E.T.K.</a></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1131862">CB03_0044</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>44</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-09'>Apr 9 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee, Esq</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In conversation with<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/93771' title='Deblois, Stephen G.'>Mr. Stephen G. Deblois</a> last Sat<span class='line-break'></span>urday I understood him to say<span class='line-break'> </span>that on the whole he was satisfied<span class='line-break'> </span>with the present access to <a href='/pages/subjects/61155' title='Coleus Path'>Coleus<span class='line-break'> </span>Path</a>, (by a small path from <a href='/pages/subjects/61302' title='Woodbine Path'>Wood<span class='line-break'></span>bine</a>,) and^<sup>that</sup> he agreed with me in<span class='line-break'> </span>thinking it on the whole a more<span class='line-break'> </span>convenient access from carriages <u>at<span class='line-break'> </span>a funeral </u> than it would be <u>down</u><span class='line-break'> </span>a flight of steps; he also said he<span class='line-break'> </span>thought it probably exposed his lot less<span class='line-break'> </span>to the risk of being run over by intruders<span class='line-break'> </span>than the steps would near his lot. He<span class='line-break'> </span>authorized me to state the above on his<span class='line-break'> </span>views.</p>
<p>very truly yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131868">CB03_0050</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I am just in<span class='line-break'> </span>receipt of a note from <a href='/pages/subjects/59191' title='Mann, Jonathan'>Mr. Jona<span class='line-break'> </span>Mann</a>, (as ag't for <a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>J.C. <p>I have heard nothing<span class='line-break'> </span>from him in answer to our proposition for<span class='line-break'> </span><u>building</u> the Tomb, and I presume he is<span class='line-break'> </span>waiting to get the other before giving his<span class='line-break'> </span>answer.</p>
<p>Yours Truly,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>, Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131870">CB03_0052</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>52</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-10'>April 10 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/95125' title='Snow, Samuel T.'>Saml T. Snow Esq</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Chairman of Comm. on Lots,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In view of the [true?]<span class='line-break'> </span>fact that many Proprietors find it<span class='line-break'> </span>economical to provide <u>wooden covers</u><span class='line-break'> </span>on valuable monuments during the<span class='line-break'> </span>winter, I have sometimes thought it<span class='line-break'> </span>might be advisable for the Corp.<span class='line-break'> </span>to do the same in the case of some<span class='line-break'> </span>lots under "<u>Perp. Care</u>" guaranteed and <span class='line-break'> </span>if it wise. I have caused a list of such<span class='line-break'> </span>"guaranteed" Lots as I thought warranted<span class='line-break'> </span>the expense, to be made^<sup>(Enclosed herewith)</sup> and these are,<span class='line-break'> </span>no doubt some "Unguaranteed" lots, on<span class='line-break'> </span>which there is a sufficient fund</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1131886">CB03_0068</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>68</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-11'>April 11 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/95125' title='Snow, Samuel T.'>S. T. Snow Esq.</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Ch'man Comm. on Lots,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I have received (<date when='1873-03-22'>March<span class='line-break'> </span>22<sup>d</sup></date>) offers from two persons who have<span class='line-break'> </span>manure for sale, and respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>refer the matter to your consideration,</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25004031' title='Cox, John'>John Cox Esq.</a></p>
<p>Foster St. <a href='/pages/subjects/53203' title='Cambridge, MA'>Cambridge</a><span class='line-break'> </span>has 15 cords of manure, which he<span class='line-break'> </span>wishes to dispose of. Has sold to<span class='line-break'> </span>Mt. Auburn Corp<sup>n</sup> before, 8 years ago.<span class='line-break'> </span>Says his is better than <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a> manure.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25004032' title='Conley, Martin'>Martin Conley</a></p>
<p>has 40 cords manure at<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25008254' title='Catholic Church, Cambridge'>Catholic Church</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/53203' title='Cambridge, MA'>Camb.</a></p>
<p>Offers it for $9.00 per cord.</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131887">
<h3><a name="page-1131887">CB03_0069</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>69</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>We have obtained most of our<span class='line-break'> </span>manure, the past year, from one<span class='line-break'> </span>Contractor in <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, for convenience<span class='line-break'> </span>in ordering, @ $10.00 per cord.<span class='line-break'> </span>but have found there is consider<span class='line-break'></span>able shrinkage (nearly 10 per ct.)<span class='line-break'> </span>in manure measured in <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a><span class='line-break'> </span>and afterwards carted 5 miles to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery.</p>
<p>Yours Truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>
</div>

<p>In regard to the<span class='line-break'> </span>supply of ground Posts, (for corners of Lots)<span class='line-break'> </span>would say, <a href='/pages/subjects/25004034' title='McDonnell &amp; Sons'>McDonnell &amp; Sons</a> of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/66737' title='Quincy, MA'>Quincy Mass.</a> have had a running<span class='line-break'> </span>contract for 10 years past (to cut in<span class='line-break'> </span>winter and send when they choose)<span class='line-break'> </span>at a cheap rate, and I think we<span class='line-break'> </span>have now a sufficient supply on hand<span class='line-break'> </span>for the coming year, so that it will<span class='line-break'> </span>not be necessary to buy anymore<span class='line-break'> </span>at present.</p>

<p><date when='1873-04-14'>April 14 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee Esq. Pres't.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I have had an in<span class='line-break'></span>vestigation made by <a href='/pages/subjects/105069' title='Shedd &amp; Sawyer'>Shedd &amp; Sawyer</a><span class='line-break'> </span>C.E. of all Lots, the inclosures of<span class='line-break'> </span>which do not agree with the <u>deeds</u> and<span class='line-break'> </span>find that there are about <u>23</u> Lots which<span class='line-break'> </span>are larger than the deeds call for, making<span class='line-break'> </span>by hasty enumeration about <u>2500</u> feet of<span class='line-break'> </span>land enclosed in Lots, more than the<span class='line-break'> </span>deeds allow, which @ $1.00 per ft. (our price<span class='line-break'> </span>for additions) would amount to about<span class='line-break'> </span>$2500.00.</p>
<p>There are also about 32 Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>where a small amount of land has<span class='line-break'> </span>been taken than the deeds call for,</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131894">
<h3><a name="page-1131894">CB03_0076</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>76</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>(about 3000 ft. of land in all.)<span class='line-break'> </span>but that, I suppose, we are not concerned<span class='line-break'> </span>about (other than to beware of setting such<span class='line-break'> </span>paces to other parties) and perhaps<span class='line-break'> </span>to require boundary posts, in some in<span class='line-break'></span>stances to be set on the true boundary<span class='line-break'> </span>lines.</p>
<p>In regard to the cases of the<span class='line-break'> </span>first class, (where the enclosures are lar<span class='line-break'></span>ger than the deeds authorize) it was<span class='line-break'> </span>my intention to call on the parties<span class='line-break'> </span>to <u> pay up</u>; and for this purpose, had<span class='line-break'> </span>prepared a draft of a circular, (which is<span class='line-break'> </span>enclosed) to the sent with a duly prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>"adjust" for the extra land.</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131896">
<h3><a name="page-1131896">CB03_0078</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>78</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-14'>April 14 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee Esq. Prest</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I send you here<span class='line-break'></span>with all the Documents in my<span class='line-break'> </span>possession connected with the <u>drainage</u><span class='line-break'> </span>of <u><a href='/pages/subjects/59904' title='Spruce Avenue'>Spruce Ave</a>.</u></p>
<p>He made a survey and<span class='line-break'> </span>took levels in <date when='1871'>Summer of '71</date>, as far<span class='line-break'> </span>as our fence but did not level at all<span class='line-break'> </span>on to <u><a href='/pages/subjects/25004456' title='Chant Lot'>"Chant Lot"</a></u> as we did not own<span class='line-break'> </span>it at the time.</p>
<p>I would respectfully re<span class='line-break'></span>commend extending the profile, now, on<span class='line-break'> </span>to the <a href='/pages/subjects/25004456' title='Chant Lot'>Chant Lot</a>; so as to make a<span class='line-break'> </span>comparison between the level of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lowest spot on said Lot and the lowest</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131897">
<h3><a name="page-1131897">CB03_0079</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>79</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>spot on <a href='/pages/subjects/59904' title='Spruce Avenue'>Spruce Avenue</a>.</p>
<p>My general idea has<span class='line-break'> </span>been, (if a sufficient difference of<span class='line-break'> </span>level should be found to exist,)<span class='line-break'> </span>that one or 2 shallow cesspools<span class='line-break'> </span>should be built in lowest part<span class='line-break'> </span>of <a href='/pages/subjects/59904' title='Spruce Avenue'>Spruce Ave</a>., with a drain starting<span class='line-break'> </span>from them at as <u>high</u> a level as<span class='line-break'> </span>possible, and leading to the lowest point<span class='line-break'> </span>in the <a href='/pages/subjects/25004456' title='Chant Lot'>"Chant Lot"</a>; where there might<span class='line-break'> </span>be built a large timber "vat" or "reservoir"<span class='line-break'> </span>(see Doc. V.) as deep as the subterranean<span class='line-break'> </span>level of water there will conveniently allow<span class='line-break'> </span>and with the outlet of the drain in it<span class='line-break'> </span>arranged as <u>low</u> as convenient, so as<span class='line-break'> </span>to give all practicable fall to the drain.</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131898">
<h3><a name="page-1131898">CB03_0080</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>80</p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>If the experiment prove a success,<span class='line-break'> </span>the timber reservoir can then be lined<span class='line-break'> </span>with stone.</p>
<p>The accompanying papers<span class='line-break'> </span>are as follows</p>
<p>Envelope I - <u>Plan</u> of <a href='/pages/subjects/59904' title='Spruce Avenue'>Spruce Ave</a>. Basin,<span class='line-break'> </span>and five (5) Profiles whose<span class='line-break'> </span>courses are marked on <u>Plan</u><span class='line-break'> </span>by corresponding letters,<span class='line-break'> </span>(N.B. The line not yet leveled<span class='line-break'> </span>over is from E to X on said <span class='line-break'> </span>Plan.)</p>
<p>Envelope II - Profile your <a href='/pages/subjects/59904' title='Spruce Avenue'>Spruce Ave</a>.<span class='line-break'> </span>cor. <a href='/pages/subjects/61104' title='Acacia Path'>Acacia Path</a> to <a href='/pages/subjects/57671' title='Forest Pond'>Forest Pond</a><span class='line-break'> </span>also <a href='/pages/subjects/60688' title='Hildreth, Mr.'> Mr. Hildreth's</a> report of<span class='line-break'> </span>work done in<date when='1871-10'> Oct. [18]71</date>,</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131901">
<h3><a name="page-1131901">CB03_0083</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>83</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-14'>April 14 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee Esq. Prest</a>,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I wish to call to your<span class='line-break'> </span>notice, the necessity of considering the<span class='line-break'> </span>needs of the Cemetery in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>a supply of <u>gravel</u> for the future.</p>
<p>According to an estimate<span class='line-break'> </span>made by <a href='/pages/subjects/25004466' title='Harrison, Mr.'>Mr. Harrison</a> about a year<span class='line-break'> </span>ago about 14,500 cu. yds would be<span class='line-break'> </span>required for grading in the vicinity<span class='line-break'> </span>of <a href='/pages/subjects/57864' title='Halcyon Lake'>Halcyon Lake</a> and 1000 cu yds<span class='line-break'> </span>to fill the <u>hollow</u> between N. &amp; S. <a href='/pages/subjects/61222' title='Lime Avenue'>Lime Aves.</a><span class='line-break'> </span>While the supply in the hill between<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/61293' title='Viburnum Avenue'>Viburnum Ave.</a> and <a href='/pages/subjects/61214' title='Kalmia Path'>Kalmia P.</a> was<span class='line-break'> </span>only about 2,250 cu. yds.</p>
<p>Since that time the <u>hollow</u><span class='line-break'> </span>between <a href='/pages/subjects/61222' title='Lime Avenue'>Lime Aves</a>, has been nearly filled<span class='line-break'> </span>thus leaving very little for the other work)</p>
<p>There is some gravel on<span class='line-break'> </span><u><a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a></u>, but not enough for</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131902">
<h3><a name="page-1131902">CB03_0084</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>84</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>the future needs of the Cemetery.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/64030' title='McDonald, Alexander'>Mr. McDonald</a> owns<span class='line-break'> </span>the nearest supply to the <a href='/pages/subjects/57664' title='Entrance Gateway'><u>front gate</u></a><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/54337' title='Stone, Mr.'>Mr. Stone</a>, the nearest to the <a href='/pages/subjects/25004469' title='Back Gate'><u>back gate</u></a></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/64030' title='McDonald, Alexander'>Mr McDonald's</a> supply lies<span class='line-break'> </span>about in the position of the rectangle<span class='line-break'> </span>a-b a-d on the <u>enclosed sketch</u>, where<span class='line-break'> </span>thus is a large quantity of gravel; some<span class='line-break'> </span>already sold to contractors, but a suf<span class='line-break'></span>ficient quantity, unsold as yet.</p>
<p>He would be glad to make<span class='line-break'> </span>an arrangement with us, either by<span class='line-break'> </span>selling us a piece of land outright, on<span class='line-break'> </span>fee simple (which we could sell when<span class='line-break'> </span>we had taken off the gravel) or by<span class='line-break'> </span>selling us the gravel off the land,</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131903">
<h3><a name="page-1131903">CB03_0085</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>85</p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>the fee to remain in him -</p>
<p>But I think he would ask<span class='line-break'> </span>nearly as much for the latter as the<span class='line-break'> </span>former.</p>
<p>I would respectfully com<span class='line-break'></span>mend this subject to the earnest con<span class='line-break'></span>sideration of the Trustees, as on<span class='line-break'> </span>supply of gravel, (as well as of loam.)<span class='line-break'> </span>is drawing low; and it will be well<span class='line-break'> </span>to consider the subject in advance<span class='line-break'> </span>of any actual deficiency.</p>
<p>Very truly Yours,<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

Should not the language<span class='line-break'> </span>be changed or explained to allow 30 ft<span class='line-break'> </span>from Lake at South end?</p>

<p><date when='1873-04-15'>April 15 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee, Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Chair Comm. on Grounds</a></p>
<p><del>Gentlemen</del>, Dear Sir</p>
<p>I present herewith my<span class='line-break'> </span>Plan of <u>Contours</u> of the <u><a href='/pages/subjects/58521' title='Watriss, William'>Watriss</a> Lot</u><span class='line-break'> </span>(A), an original rough draft of<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues and Paths for same (B), and<span class='line-break'> </span>a Plan of the Avenues as now staked<span class='line-break'> </span>out on the ground (C).</p>
<p>The Lot was Cross-Section<span class='line-break'> </span>in the winter of '71 - '72, stakes being<span class='line-break'> </span>driven down at corners of squares of<span class='line-break'> </span>50 ft and levels taken at each stake,<span class='line-break'> </span>and from these the Contour Plan (A)<span class='line-break'> </span>was made.</p>
<p>The Avenues were staked<span class='line-break'> </span>out in the summer of '72 under the</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131911">
<h3><a name="page-1131911">CB03_0093</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>93</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>personal supervisor of the Supt.</p>
<p>Posts 3 ft out of ground,<span class='line-break'> </span>were set at all prominent points,<span class='line-break'> </span>and long stakes, firmly driven down,<span class='line-break'> </span>were put in to complete the lines.</p>
<p>Both posts and stakes were<span class='line-break'> </span>painted, those in the lines of the<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues - <u>white</u> and those marking<span class='line-break'> </span>the Ornamental Grounds - Yellow -</p>
<p>The lot is scattered over<span class='line-break'> </span>with large piles of Muck, among<span class='line-break'> </span>which the Avenues have been kept clear,<span class='line-break'> </span>but not built as yet, except a portion<span class='line-break'> </span>of <a href='/pages/subjects/61299' title='Western Avenue'>Western Avenue</a> (from (K) to (L) [Plan of<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues (C)]), which has been graded suf<span class='line-break'></span>ficiently to enable a carriage to be driven<span class='line-break'> </span>over it.</p>
<p>The <u>muck</u> which has been<span class='line-break'> </span>[omited?] on having now had a whole</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131912">
<h3><a name="page-1131912">CB03_0094</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>94</p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>years exposure, might be spread out<span class='line-break'> </span>and then plowed in.</p>
<p>This arrangement of<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues has been made, starting<span class='line-break'> </span>with the idea of one or two main <u>car<span class='line-break'></span>riage ways </u>, of gentle curvature and<span class='line-break'> </span>easy grade, following the natural curves<span class='line-break'> </span>of the ground, with as easy a slope as<span class='line-break'> </span>possible, and encircling the best portion<span class='line-break'> </span>of the land.</p>
<p>Everything else has been<span class='line-break'> </span>made subsidiary to the idea of a pleas<span class='line-break'></span>ant drive, as Paths will take care of<span class='line-break'> </span>themselves; and any small irregular<span class='line-break'> </span>lots, left at corners of paths, or between<span class='line-break'> </span>regular square lots, will sell even</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131913">
<h3><a name="page-1131913">CB03_0095</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>95</p>
<p>(4)</p>
<p>more readily and profitably than the<span class='line-break'> </span>common square lots.</p>
<p>Great care has also been<span class='line-break'> </span>taken to spare all of the few trees now<span class='line-break'> </span>left on this piece of ground.</p>
<p>The ground next South<span class='line-break'> </span>of the <a href='/pages/subjects/57664' title='Entrance Gateway'>Main Entrance</a> to the lot from<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/61175' title='Elm Avenue'>Elm Avenue</a>, I think, is very well suited<span class='line-break'> </span>to a <u><a href='/pages/subjects/61319' title='Public Lot'>public Lot</a></u>. (The only one we have<span class='line-break'> </span>now vacant for use (<a href='/pages/subjects/61319' title='Public Lot'>St. Paul lot</a>) is rather<span class='line-break'> </span>far from the Entrance for those who usually<span class='line-break'> </span>resort to a <a href='/pages/subjects/61319' title='Public Lot'>public Lot</a>, and who come in<span class='line-break'> </span>on foot.)</p>
<p>A <u><a href='/pages/subjects/25004485' title='summer - house'>summer - house</a></u> or open<span class='line-break'> </span>place with seats, would also be very ap<span class='line-break'></span>propriate near such a lot.<span class='line-break'> </span>N.B. - The subject of the exit and entrance<span class='line-break'> </span>to the <a href='/pages/subjects/58521' title='Watriss, William'>Watriss</a> lot, I will make the subject of<span class='line-break'> </span>future letter.</p>

<p>We have been in the<span class='line-break'> </span>habit of buying it from our own<span class='line-break'> </span>men in similar cases, but I<span class='line-break'> </span>do not think we have paid quite<span class='line-break'> </span>so much.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131916">CB03_0098</a></h3>

<p>98</p>
<p>(1)</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-15'>Apr, 15, [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25004529' title='Moore, Hollis'>Hollis Moore, Esq</a>,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>On going by your<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25004528' title='Lot 4046'>Tomb<!--4046--></a> on Friday last, I noticed<span class='line-break'> </span>that your <u>Cap</u> had been<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered. It is very<span class='line-break'> </span>well cut indeed, but it seems,<span class='line-break'> </span>that in carting it in, the<span class='line-break'> </span>wagon slipped, or the cap<span class='line-break'> </span>slipped from the wagon<span class='line-break'> </span>some way fell down the hill,<span class='line-break'> </span>and a considerable chip<span class='line-break'> </span>was knocked out on the<span class='line-break'> </span>right hand upper edge of<span class='line-break'> </span>the top.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25004489' title='Gilman, Mr.'>Mr Gilman</a></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131917">
<h3><a name="page-1131917">CB03_0099</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>99</p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>[diagram: stone cap of tomb in <a href='/pages/subjects/25004528' title='lot 4046'>lot 4046</a> inscribed with <a href='/pages/subjects/25004529' title='Moore, Hollis'>"H.M"</a> indicating "chip" on right side]</p>
<p>[diagram: cap bottom (rectangle) split into 3 parts indicating "chip" on right front]</p>
<p>came to see me this morning<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; proposed to leave it to me to pay<span class='line-break'> </span>what should be done; but I told him<span class='line-break'> </span>that was beyond any province,<span class='line-break'> </span>but I would write you about it.</p>
<p>It is a pity as the<span class='line-break'> </span>cap is a fine stone &amp; beautifully<span class='line-break'> </span>cut. The only way<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131918">
<h3><a name="page-1131918">CB03_0100</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>100</p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>to cure it that I know of is<span class='line-break'> </span>to cut a <u>draft</u> or <u>moulding</u><span class='line-break'> </span>to lean around the outside of the<span class='line-break'> </span>cap, thus, -</p>
<p>[diagram: same drawings of <a href='/pages/subjects/25004528' title='lot 4046'>lot 4046</a> as on previous page; shows moulding placement]</p>

<div id="page-1131919">
<h3><a name="page-1131919">CB03_0101</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>101</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-15'>Apr 15, [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee Esq. Prest.</a><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>There are a number of <u>Signs</u> very<span class='line-break'> </span>much wanted in Mount Auburn, partly on new grounds not yet<span class='line-break'> </span>fully occupied, and partly on old grounds where they have been<span class='line-break'> </span>overlooked -</p>
<p>For the newer parts, I would suggest the <u>cast-iron<span class='line-break'> </span>signs</u>; for the older parts, <u>wooden ones,</u> of which we have a quan<span class='line-break'></span>tity on hand - <span class='line-break'> </span>The last iron ones were bought in <date when='1868'>1868</date>,^<sup><date when='1869'>or '69</date></sup> at a cost of about I think<span class='line-break'> </span>$4.00 each.</p>
<p>I have understood from <a href='/pages/subjects/25004499' title='Bramhall, O., Mr.'>Mr. O. Bramhal</a>l of <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, that<span class='line-break'> </span>he had the patterns from which those purchased were cast; (that<span class='line-break'> </span>however was before the great fire, when his shop in Congress St<span class='line-break'> </span>was burnt).</p>
<p>We have at the <a href='/pages/subjects/105109' title='Carpenter shop'>Carpenters shop</a> about [blank space] wooden</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131920">
<h3><a name="page-1131920">CB03_0102</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>102</p>
<p>2</p>
<p>signs painted, but not lettered; and about [space] locust posts ready<span class='line-break'> </span>painted for the purpose.<span class='line-break'> </span>With a view to make a thorough job of this matter, I had the grounds<span class='line-break'> </span>examined by a clerk <a href='/pages/subjects/25004501' title='Minot, Mr.'>(Mr Minot)</a> in 1870, and a list made of the<span class='line-break'> </span>signs now up, and also those needed, which I enclose.</p>
<p>I also had the grounds examined by <a href='/pages/subjects/25004466' title='Harrison, Mr.'>Mr Harrison</a> in 1872, <span class='line-break'> </span>and a map marked with the position of those now in, which I also<span class='line-break'> </span>enclose.</p>
<p>I would respectfully recommend that the wooden signs should be<span class='line-break'> </span>lettered and some iron ones bought, as soon as consistent-with con<span class='line-break'></span>[?] please find a list of enclosed.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>107</p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>until now require to be moved<span class='line-break'> </span>probably the sooner the better, that<span class='line-break'> </span>is at the proper season of the year<span class='line-break'> </span>and for this reason it seems necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>to decide soon where they shall be<span class='line-break'> </span>let out.</p>
<p>This arrangement of Aves.<span class='line-break'> </span>(Plan [G]) has been made, starting<span class='line-break'> </span>with the idea of two or three <u>main<span class='line-break'> </span>carriage drives</u> of gentle curvature<span class='line-break'> </span>and easy grade, following the nat<span class='line-break'></span>ural curves, of the Ground, with as<span class='line-break'> </span>easy a slope as possible, and en<span class='line-break'></span>circling the best position of the land.</p>

<p>(over)</p>

<div class="page-content">
<p>108</p>
<p>(4)</p>
<p><u>pleasant drive</u> as paths will<span class='line-break'> </span>take care of themselves; and any<span class='line-break'> </span>small irregular lots, left at cor<span class='line-break'></span>ners of paths, or between regular<span class='line-break'> </span>square lots, will sell even more<span class='line-break'> </span>readily and profitably than the<span class='line-break'> </span>common square lots.</p>
<p>The leading idea in this<span class='line-break'> </span>plan is <a href='/pages/subjects/61172' title='Eagle Avenue'><u>Eagle Ave</u></a> to be <u>broad</u> and<span class='line-break'> </span>of easy curve and grade, forming<span class='line-break'> </span>an easy and picturesque access to<span class='line-break'> </span>the grounds from <a href='/pages/subjects/25004469' title='Back Gate'>the back gate</a>, and<span class='line-break'> </span>in full view of the <a href='/pages/subjects/54814' title='Washington Tower'>Tower</a> and its<span class='line-break'> </span>terraces.</p>

<p>The point of entrance to<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a> are pretty much entirely<span class='line-break'> </span>fixed now, by the sale of lots along<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/61227' title='Magnolia Avenue'>Magnolia Ave</a>, blocking up all but<span class='line-break'> </span>a few points.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131934">CB03_0116</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='116'>116</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-16'>April 16<sup>th</sup>, 1873</date>.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee Esq. President</a>,</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Enclosed please find documents<span class='line-break'> </span>relative to "<u>Birds</u>"</p>
<p>The following list I enclose;<span class='line-break'> </span>1<sup>st</sup> Swans from <a href='/pages/subjects/65979' title='Cincinnati, OH'>Cincinnati</a><span class='line-break'> </span>2<sup>nd</sup> <a href='/pages/subjects/95421' title='Forest Hills Cemetery, Jamaica Plain'>Forest Hills</a> Poland Ducks (croppld crowns)<span class='line-break'> </span>3<sup>rd</sup> Cayuga Duck<span class='line-break'> </span>4<sup>th</sup> Food of Swans<span class='line-break'> </span>5<sup>th</sup> Extracts from J.M Bechstein "Cage &amp; Chamber Birds"<span class='line-break'> </span>6<sup>th</sup> Documents relating to "<a href='/pages/subjects/57835' title='Black, James'>Black</a> cap" Warblers</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<div id="page-1131935">
<h3><a name="page-1131935">CB03_0117</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='117'>117</span></p>
<p>April 16 1873</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee Esq. Prest.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In connection with<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter of "Reservations" (see letter<span class='line-break'> </span>of April 15) I would say that the<span class='line-break'> </span>only way in which an unpracticed<span class='line-break'> </span>person can distinguish them is by<span class='line-break'> </span>their color on the "Sectional Plan";<span class='line-break'> </span>and as several are not yet colored.</p>
<p>viz - "<span class='line-break'> </span>1 - " lot in front of <a href='/pages/subjects/53239' title='Bigelow Chapel'>Chapel</a>"<span class='line-break'> </span>2 - " <a href='/pages/subjects/58208' title='Alice Fountain'>Alice Fountain</a>, "Reservation"<span class='line-break'> </span>3 - " Land around <a href='/pages/subjects/57593' title='Auburn Lake'>Auburn Lake</a>"<span class='line-break'> </span>4  -" Reservation of the Mound."</p>
<p>I would respectfully recommend that <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/105069' title='Shedd &amp; Sawyer'>Shedd &amp; Sawyer</a> be requested<span class='line-break'> </span>to [attend?] to this as soon as possible.</p>
<p>Respy <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131936">
<h3><a name="page-1131936">CB03_0118</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='118'>118</span></p>
<p>(1)</p>
<p><date when='1873-04-16'>April 16 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee</a> Esq. Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I send you here<span class='line-break'></span>with a portfolio containing Architects'<span class='line-break'> </span>Plans of <u><a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'>New Receiving Tomb</a></u>, <span class='line-break'> </span>also four "Rolled Plans."</p>
<p>viz - 1<sup>st</sup> Section of Tomb showing<span class='line-break'> </span>fronts of <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a> <u>as actually built</u><span class='line-break'> </span>2<sup>d</sup> - Cross section of Tomb, through<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a>, <u>as actually built</u> (except<span class='line-break'> </span>Tile Floor not yet laid.)<span class='line-break'> </span>3<sup>d</sup> - Plan of Vicinity of Tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>showing <u>possibilities</u> of enlargement<span class='line-break'> </span>4<sup>th</sup> Also Plan of Vicinity of Tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>not so extended.</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131937">
<h3><a name="page-1131937">CB03_0119</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='119'>119</span></p>
<p>(2)</p>
<p>In <u>Plan <a href='/pages/subjects/64179' title='Lot 1'>No. 1</a></u> the colored portion<span class='line-break'> </span>represents the Section of <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a><span class='line-break'> </span>built previous to<date when='1871-12-31'> Dec 31, [18]71</date> with a<span class='line-break'> </span>partial [?] the Vestibule - enclosedportion being a design for extension<span class='line-break'> </span><u>Plan No. 2</u> [Election of same?]<span class='line-break'> </span><u>Plan Nos. 3 &amp; 4</u> show open spaces in<span class='line-break'> </span>vicinity of Tomb, into which it may be<span class='line-break'> </span>extended almost indefinitely; and<span class='line-break'> </span>for the policy pursued, or <a href='/pages/subjects/95421' title='Forest Hills Cemetery, Jamaica Plain'>Forest<span class='line-break'> </span>Hills Cemetery</a> Corp<sup>n</sup> is a wise one -<span class='line-break'> </span>(their Rec. Tomb [rough sketch enclosed]<span class='line-break'> </span>contains <u>286 Catacombs</u> against<span class='line-break'> </span><u>30</u> in or is so far as built,) - there<span class='line-break'> </span>seems to be no doubt that more ac<span class='line-break'></span>commodations will at sometime be<span class='line-break'> </span>required here; and as the same<span class='line-break'> </span>Entrance and Vestibule will serve<span class='line-break'> </span>for a Tomb of any size, it seems</p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131938">
<h3><a name="page-1131938">CB03_0120</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='120'>120</span></p>
<p>(3)</p>
<p>now advisable to extend the present<span class='line-break'> </span>structure than to build another or others<span class='line-break'> </span>in other parts of the grounds, with<span class='line-break'> </span>further expense for suitable approaches<span class='line-break'> </span>and fronts.</p>
<p>Besides these plans, we<span class='line-break'> </span>have a set of "Detailed" or "Working<span class='line-break'> </span>Lots" of stonework &amp;c, which would be<span class='line-break'> </span>required in the construction of the next<span class='line-break'> </span>Section of <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a> (50), as represented<span class='line-break'> </span>in Plan No. 1 (nearly 20 Plans in all)<span class='line-break'> </span>also a statement of all materials and<span class='line-break'> </span>quantities of each, that would be re<span class='line-break'></span>quired for same. (These were prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>in summer of 1872 by <a href='/pages/subjects/25004466' title='Harrison, Mr.'>Mr. Harrison</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>draughtsman, since deceased).</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='121'>121</span></p>

<p>As <a href='/pages/subjects/54338' title='Indian Ridge Path'>Indian Ridge Path</a> crosses<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'><!--Receiving-->Tomb</a>, over the <u>next</u> section of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>catacombs</a> to be built, a ventilator<span class='line-break'> </span>cannot be put there; but would come<span class='line-break'> </span>appropriately over the <u>next but one</u>,<span class='line-break'> </span>which in my plan I have supposed<span class='line-break'> </span>to be left vacant for the present, with<span class='line-break'> </span>a side arch turned on either side<span class='line-break'> </span>for a future side extension.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/79902' title='Lot 424'>Lot #424</a>, represented<span class='line-break'> </span>in the engraved map of Mt. Auburn,<span class='line-break'> </span>just east of the <a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'>Rec. Tomb</a>, and<span class='line-break'> </span>north side of <a href='/pages/subjects/54338' title='Indian Ridge Path'>I. Ridge path</a>, <u>no longer<span class='line-break'> </span>exists</u>; it having been originally<span class='line-break'> </span>deeded to <a href='/pages/subjects/25006685' title='Francis, D.'>D. Francis</a> in 1834, and</p>
<p>(over)</p>

<p>back again to Corp'n <date when='1850-09-27'>Sept. 27 [18]50</date>.</p>
<p>Two Designs for <u>Iron<span class='line-break'> </span>doors</u> prepared in 1872 by <a href='/pages/subjects/57479' title='Bryant, Gridley J. F.'>Mr. G.<span class='line-break'> </span>J. F. <div id="page-1131941">
<h3><a name="page-1131941">CB03_0123</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='123'>123</span></p>
<p>(6)</p>
<p>The marble doors (and brass<span class='line-break'> </span>handles for same,) for the <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a><span class='line-break'> </span>now in, are stowed at <a href='/pages/subjects/102074' title='Engine house'>Engine House</a><span class='line-break'> </span>attic.</p>
<p>Notes will be found on file<span class='line-break'> </span>of the size of various <u>coffin boxes</u><span class='line-break'> </span>which we have had on hand for<span class='line-break'> </span>interment; and of the opinion of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/105156' title='Stafford, Mr.'>Mr. Safford, our Undertaker</a>; from<span class='line-break'> </span>which it will be seen that every<span class='line-break'> </span>thing points to the necessity of making<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a> <u>higher and wider</u>, in<span class='line-break'> </span>any increase of the Tomb.</p>
<p>My plan for the next set,<span class='line-break'> </span>you will notice, provides for this, and <span class='line-break'> </span>still leaves the cornice at same hight [sic],<span class='line-break'> </span>for uniform effect.</p>
<p>(over)</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131942">
<h3><a name="page-1131942">CB03_0124</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='124'>124</span></p>
<p>(7)</p>
<p>After passing the side<span class='line-break'> </span>archways, the cornice of the <a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'><!--Receiving-->Tomb</a><span class='line-break'> </span>might be <u>raised</u>, I think, without<span class='line-break'> </span>injuring the effect; and thus any<span class='line-break'> </span>desired size of <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>Catacombs</a> be<span class='line-break'> </span>obtained.</p>
<p>Above mentioned papers<span class='line-break'> </span>and several others, (<u>viz Envelopes</u><span class='line-break'> </span>endorsed with contents) are enclosed<span class='line-break'> </span>also sketch of Rec. Tomb (Plan) at <a href='/pages/subjects/95421' title='Forest Hills Cemetery, Jamaica Plain'>Forest<span class='line-break'> </span>Hills Cem.</a></p>
<p>Truly Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>C.W. Folsom</a>,<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131943">CB03_0125</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='125'>125</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-15'>April 15 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee Esq. Prest</a>.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I send you here<span class='line-break'> </span>with the papers in my possession,<span class='line-break'> </span>connected with the <u>raising of the grade<span class='line-break'> </span>and building new <a href='/pages/subjects/54812' title='Perimeter Fence'>Iron fence on<span class='line-break'> </span>Mt. Auburn St.</a></u> in front of <a href='/pages/subjects/58521' title='Watriss, William'>Watriss</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Lot, in autumn of 1871.</p>
<p>I do not know of anything<span class='line-break'> </span>connected with the work that was<span class='line-break'> </span>left unfinished.</p>
<p>The papers are a "Profile" of<span class='line-break'> </span>the past of <u> Mt. Auburn St. </u> in question and<span class='line-break'> </span>the contents of four Envelopes.<span class='line-break'> </span>I) - abstract of <a href='/pages/subjects/25006704' title='G.W. &amp; F. Smith'>G.W. &amp; F. Smith's</a></p>
<p>(over)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div id="page-1131947">
<h3><a name="page-1131947">CB03_0129</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='129'>129</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-16'>April 16<sup>th</sup> 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25006717' title='Richards, Joseph R.'>Joseph R Richards Esq</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Your favor of 17<sup>th</sup> inst is rec<sup>d</sup> for<span class='line-break'> </span>an order for having your lot graded &amp; corner posts set.<span class='line-break'> </span>As to the latter I would suggest as being more ornamented<span class='line-break'> </span>to hexagonal Posts if agreeable to you to have them.</p>
<p>Presuming you w<sup>d</sup> wish your lot sodded &amp; No. cut<span class='line-break'> </span>on Posts I have enclosed an order for same which will<span class='line-break'> </span>you please sign &amp; return to me.</p>
<p>There are two styles of putting N<sup>os</sup> on post viz<span class='line-break'> </span>plain &amp; square sunk. The cost of the former being $3.00/100<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; the latter $6.00/100</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</a><span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1131948">
<h3><a name="page-1131948">CB03_0130</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='130'>130</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-18'>April 18<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J. T. Bradlee</a> Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I find it has been<span class='line-break'> </span>customary to keep back a part <span class='line-break'> </span>of the pay of many of the men,<span class='line-break'> </span>under what is known as the<span class='line-break'> </span>"Bounty System", till the close of<span class='line-break'> </span>the season.</p>
<p>Is it considered desirable to<span class='line-break'> </span>continue this custom? I am<span class='line-break'> </span>inclined to believe that it<span class='line-break'> </span>causes considerable dissatisfaction<span class='line-break'> </span>and not entirely without reason.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></a></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-18'>April 18 [187]3.</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee</a> Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I have examined <span class='line-break'> </span>the Path so called, on the East<span class='line-break'> </span>of the <a href='/pages/subjects/57664' title='Entrance Gateway'>Main Entrance</a> to Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>and I estimate the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>ploughing, levelling, sowing with<span class='line-break'> </span>grass seed &amp; rolling at ($140.)<span class='line-break'> </span>one hundred &amp; forty dollars, tho'<span class='line-break'> </span>it is possible perhaps to do it<span class='line-break'> </span>a little less.</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131949">
<h3><a name="page-1131949">CB03_0133</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='133'>133</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-21'>April 21 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25006746' title='Blanchard, John A.'>J.A. Blanchard Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>In Nov. last you were re<span class='line-break'></span>quested, by letter, to inform us whether you<span class='line-break'> </span>wished to retain the space between your <a href='/pages/subjects/25006720' title='Lot 851'>lot<span class='line-break'> </span>#851</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/61175' title='Elm Avenue'>Elm Ave.</a> and <a href='/pages/subjects/25006721' title='Lot 689'>#689</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25006722' title='Sargent, H. B.'>H. B. Sargent Propr.</a><span class='line-break'> </span>as we had an application to sell it, and ad<span class='line-break'></span>joining Proprs. have the privilege (by the Bye Laws)<span class='line-break'> </span>of buying such spaces in preference to other<span class='line-break'> </span>purchasers.</p>
<p>We have never rec'd. your reply<span class='line-break'> </span>and having since had another application for the<span class='line-break'> </span>land, would be greatly obliged if you will in<span class='line-break'></span>form us at your earliest convenience, whether<span class='line-break'> </span>you wish to take the space or not.</p>
<p>Resp'y Yours <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering Supt.</a><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25006734' title='K., E. T. Staff'>Per E.T.K.</a></p>
