<p>The order is received<span class='line-break'> </span>and in reply I would say that<span class='line-break'> </span>we can grade, sod lot &amp; cut no for<span class='line-break'> </span>$125, furnishing you such corner<span class='line-break'> </span>posts as we keep a supply of -</p>

<p><a href='/pages/subjects/95125' title='Snow, Samuel T.'>Sam<sup>l</sup> T. Snow Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dr Sir,</p>

<p>I thought I would let him<span class='line-break'> </span>take his orders for care direct<span class='line-break'> </span>from myself, only calling on the<span class='line-break'> </span>gardener to furnish the necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>number of plants, thus making it<span class='line-break'> </span>a separate department. Please let<span class='line-break'> </span>me know as soon as convenient<span class='line-break'> </span>your wishes in the matter</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt</a></p>

<h3><a name="page-1131962">CB03_0147</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='147'>147</span></p>
<p><u><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering</a></u></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-25'>April [25?] 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25006747' title='Ripley, Isaac H.'>Isaac H. Ripley</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Your letter of April 23<sup>d</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>inquiring for a Lot. to accommodate 6 graves<span class='line-break'> </span>was rec'd. In reply I would say there is a<span class='line-break'> </span>desirable lot on <a href='/pages/subjects/61143' title='Camellia Path'>Camellia Path</a>, next East of [?]<span class='line-break'> </span>10 ft front by 20 ft deep, area 200 sq. ft @ $1.25<span class='line-break'> </span>per sq. ft for the land. Grading, &amp;c extra of course<span class='line-break'> </span>say about $100.00 more or less</p>
<p>Land - $250.00<span class='line-break'> </span>Deed - 2.00<span class='line-break'> </span>Grading &amp;c - 100.00</p>
<p>Also a rear lot between <a href='/pages/subjects/61188' title='Gerardia Path'>Gerardia <!--P--></a> and <a href='/pages/subjects/61290' title='Vernonia Path'>Vernonia Paths</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Area 1150 sq. ft. <u>Price</u> <u>Complete</u> $325.00</p>
<p>Respectfully Yours<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Supt.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131966">CB03_0151</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='151'>151</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-04-29'>April 29<sup>th</sup> 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/73016' title='Barker, Alexander Augustus'>A.A. Barker Esq</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>On page 35 of the By-Laws<span class='line-break'> </span>"Seventh" (of Form from Conveyance for Lots)<span class='line-break'> </span>you will see "That if any monument or Effigy<span class='line-break'> </span>or any structure whatever, or any inscription be<span class='line-break'> </span>placed in or upon the said land, which shall<span class='line-break'> </span>be determined by the major part of said Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>for time being to be offensive or improper, the<span class='line-break'> </span>said Trustees or the major part of them, shall<span class='line-break'> </span>have the right + it shall be their duty, to enter<span class='line-break'> </span>upon said land + remove the same offensive<span class='line-break'> </span>or improper object or objects"</p>
<p>By special direction of Trustees I am<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] to <u>strictly</u> enforce this law, and to<span class='line-break'> </span>entrust all placards or notices calling attention<span class='line-break'> </span>to lots for sale [of such?] objects</p>
<p>I therefore request you <u>promptly</u> + <span class='line-break'> </span><u>in all cases</u> to remove all such objects or<span class='line-break'> </span>notices in the grounds of the Cemetery.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1131975">CB03_0161</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

<p><date when='1873-05-05'>May 5 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25006722' title='Sargent, H. B.'>H.B. Sargeant</a> Esq.</p>
<p>D Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor <span class='line-break'> </span>of <date when='1873-04-23'>April 23<sup>rd</sup></date> The facts in regard to<span class='line-break'> </span>the space between your lot &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/25006746' title='Blanchard, John A.'>Mr <!--J.A.-->Blanchard</a><span class='line-break'> </span>are these.</p>
<p>There is room enough for a small<span class='line-break'> </span>lot there, but by the by laws you + <a href='/pages/subjects/25006746' title='Blanchard, John A.'>Mr. <!--J.A.--><span class='line-break'> </span>Blanchard</a> have the right to purchase<span class='line-break'> </span>if you see fit.  <a href='/pages/subjects/25006746' title='Blanchard, John A.'>Mr. <!--J.A.-->B.</a> has expressed<span class='line-break'> </span>his desire to take a part or all<span class='line-break'> </span>of the space between lots, leaving<span class='line-break'> </span>a passageway of 3 feet between this<span class='line-break'> </span>addition + your lot. If you don't desire<span class='line-break'> </span>to purchase I shall sell to him + <span class='line-break'> </span>he will add it to his present <a href='/pages/subjects/25006763' title='lot 1857'>lot 1857</a>.</p>
<p>If neither of you take it, I shall</p>
<p>sell to <a href='/pages/subjects/25006764' title='Dickerson, Mr.'>Mr. Dickerson</a> of <a href='/pages/subjects/53203' title='Cambridge, MA'>Cambridge</a><span class='line-break'> </span>who wishes to buy it for a small lot.</p>
<p>Please let me know whether<span class='line-break'> </span>you have any desire to take any<span class='line-break'> </span>of it that I may be prepared to<span class='line-break'> </span>act with  <a href='/pages/subjects/25006746' title='Blanchard, John A.'>Mr <!--J.A.-->Blanchard</a> -</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='162'>162</span></p>
<p><u><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering</a></u></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-06'>6 May 1873</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007366' title='Parson, J., Jr.'>J. Parsons Jr Esq</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>On looking over your arbor [vitae?]<span class='line-break'> </span>hedge I find it will be necessary to substitute eighteen new plants<span class='line-break'> </span>at a cost of $1.00/100 each, making the expense of putting the<span class='line-break'> </span>Hedge in good order $18.00/100 (eighteen dollars).</p>
<p>The price of preparing two graves on you Lot &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>planting myrtle thereon will be $16.00/100 (sixteen dollars).</p>
<p>Should you wish us to do the above work an<span class='line-break'> </span>early order will oblige</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>Jas W. Lovering</a>, Supt<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25006742' title='A. C., Per'>Per A. C.</a></p>

<h3><a name="page-1131977">CB03_0163</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='163'>163</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-06'>May 6 [187]3</date></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>The last edition of the<span class='line-break'> </span>"Guides" was published by <a href='/pages/subjects/25007368' title='Russell &amp; Richardson'>Russell &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>Richardson</a> of <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, in 1867, being<span class='line-break'> </span>made up from several old guides &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>with some additions.</p>
<p>These guides were furnished to<span class='line-break'> </span>the gate keeper @ 20<sup>Â¢</sup> each by <a href='/pages/subjects/25007368' title='Russell &amp; Richardson'>Russell<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; Richardson</a> &amp; were [?] by him<span class='line-break'> </span>at 30<sup>Â¢</sup>. A boy was employed to sell<span class='line-break'> </span>them at times, receiving 5<sup>Â¢</sup> per copy.</p>
<p>Whatever was made over the 20<sup>Â¢</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>was profit to the gate keeper.</p>
<p>The sales the last year were about<span class='line-break'> </span>500 copies, a smaller number than<span class='line-break'> </span>in previous years. Guide is now out of print<span class='line-break'> </span>I understand. Yours truly <a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a>, Supt<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/70476' title='Mackintosh, Henry B.'>HB Mackintosh</a> Esq. Treaur.</p>
</div>

<div class="page-content">

<p><date when='1873-05-10'>May 10 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25004529' title='Moore, Hollis'>Hollis Moore</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/73016' title='Barker, Alexander Augustus'>Mr Barker</a> decides that<span class='line-break'> </span>the stone is "fit to rise." The Cap after<span class='line-break'> </span>being dressed off will project an inch<span class='line-break'> </span>or a little more, the plan calling for 1 1/2 inches.</p>
<p>The marble we can provide for<span class='line-break'> </span>best by raising it from the ground.,<span class='line-break'> </span>and I think there is no danger of <span class='line-break'> </span>any injury in that way.</p>
<p>Yours very truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a></p>
<p><date when='1878-05-12'>May 12 [187]3</date></p>

<p>In sending you<span class='line-break'> </span>a new list of "plain sunk" numbers<span class='line-break'> </span>to be cut, I will request you to<span class='line-break'> </span>furnish us with good, clear, figures<span class='line-break'> </span>cut in a workmanlike manner,<span class='line-break'> </span>and to return these slips to my<span class='line-break'> </span>office marked finished with<span class='line-break'> </span>your monthly bill or <u>oftener</u></p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a></p>
<p>P.S. I notice you discount us only<span class='line-break'> </span>5% against 10% last year. I suppose<span class='line-break'> </span>you will expect the same discount<span class='line-break'> </span>on work done by us for you.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1131988">CB03_0174</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='174'>174</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-21'>May 21<sup>st</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007467' title='Morrison, C. E.'>C.E. Morrison Esq.</a></p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of the <date when='1873-06-13'>13<sup>th</sup> inst</date><span class='line-break'> </span>at hand, and I would say in reply that<span class='line-break'> </span>the four <a href='/pages/subjects/25007468' title='Lot 4190'>lots 4190</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/25007469' title='Lot 4191'><!--419-->1.</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007470' title='Lot 4192'><!--419-->2.</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007471' title='Lot 4193'><!--419-->3</a>, with additional space<span class='line-break'> </span>make 1473 feet, which you can divide<span class='line-break'> </span>into four lots. 3 of 368 feet each = 1104<span class='line-break'> </span>and one lot of  369 feet - 369<span class='line-break'> </span>making a total of 1473 sq feet. So that <span class='line-break'> </span>all that is necessary is for you to take<span class='line-break'> </span>the space &amp; make the application.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007472' title='Baker, Mr.'>Mr Baker</a> has an order from one to <span class='line-break'> </span>put the sod in order.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p><date when='1873-05-22'>May 22 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007473' title='Stevens, Moses'>Moses Stevens</a> Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a></p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>In looking up<span class='line-break'> </span>the matter of the space between your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot and the curbed lot next East, I <span class='line-break'> </span>can see no remedy for the thing unless<span class='line-break'> </span>the slope of the bank is made more graded<span class='line-break'> </span>which would bring it onto your lot, and I <span class='line-break'> </span>suppose you would not consent to having<span class='line-break'> </span>your posts moved, and making the lot<span class='line-break'> </span>smaller. The bank as now sloped is too<span class='line-break'> </span>steep for a sod to remain long.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1131989">
<h3><a name="page-1131989">CB03_0175</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='175'>175</span></p>
<p><date when=''>May 22 [187]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/105069' title='Shedd &amp; Sawyer'>Shed &amp; Sawyer</a></p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>
<p>The matter of a new map<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Cemetery is under consideration,<span class='line-break'> </span>have an estimate for the probable cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of altering our stone &amp; publishing a new edition,<span class='line-break'> </span>and I should be glad to have your figures<span class='line-break'> </span>as to the cost of preparing a plan on same<span class='line-break'> </span>scale as that of <u>1864</u>, that is, of adding to<span class='line-break'> </span>one of the present lithographs, all new lots<span class='line-break'> </span>sold since 1864, and some few paths &amp;c - The<span class='line-break'> </span>number of lots would be about 500. This<span class='line-break'> </span>includes no work on <a href='/pages/subjects/25004456' title='Chant Lot'>Chant</a> or <a href='/pages/subjects/25007476' title='Watriss Lot'>Watriss Lots</a>, or<span class='line-break'> </span>on <a href='/pages/subjects/53229' title='Stone Farm'>Stone Farm</a>.</p>
<p>Ys respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-22'>May 22 [187]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/105069' title='Shedd &amp; Sawyer'>Shed &amp; Sawyer</a></p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>Please let me have a <span class='line-break'> </span>sketch made of <a href='/pages/subjects/25007477' title='Lot 3116'>lots 3116</a> and<a href='/pages/subjects/25007478' title='Lot 2031'> 2031 </a>as now<span class='line-break'> </span>posted, also representing the old lot lines. They<span class='line-break'> </span>have been united into one lot, and a path<span class='line-break'> </span>formerly between has been [thrown?] to the N. side,<span class='line-break'> </span>I would like the cost of this ^<sup>plan</sup> on bill as we charge<span class='line-break'> </span>it to proprietor.</p>
<p>At the junction of the two branches of <a href='/pages/subjects/61251' title='Palm Avenue'>Palm Ave.</a><span class='line-break'> </span>there is a small piece of ornamental ground<span class='line-break'> </span>which has been sold with lot on corner. I<span class='line-break'> </span>would like a sketch (very rough) and the<span class='line-break'> </span>quantity of land.</p>
<p>Please attend to these matters as soon<span class='line-break'> </span>as you can &amp; oblige.</p>
<p>Yrs truly <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>

<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007423' title='Foster, William H.'>W<sup>m</sup> H. Foster Esq</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>I am in receipt of your favor of <date when='1873-05-22'>22 May.</date><span class='line-break'> </span>With regard to your request contained in your letter of <date when='1873-05-15'>15<sup>th</sup> inst</date><span class='line-break'> </span>I understood you to ask for an estimate for painting the fence &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>setting up post of <a href='/pages/subjects/25007424' title='Lot 481'>Lot #481</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/61127' title='Beech Avenue'>Beech Av.</a> only, without taking into<span class='line-break'> </span>consideration any repairs on <a href='/pages/subjects/25007479' title='Lot 474'>Lot #474</a> which adjoins the former.<span class='line-break'> </span>Presuming you wish the post to be straightened &amp; the fence<span class='line-break'> </span>around both <a href='/pages/subjects/25007479' title='Lot 474'>lots viz #474</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007424' title='Lot 481'>&amp; #481</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/61127' title='Beech Avenue'>Beech Av </a>to be painted the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost thereof will be $15.<sup>00/100</sup> for doing which work I enclose an<span class='line-break'> </span>order which will you please sign &amp; return to me. The regular charge<span class='line-break'> </span>for care of Lots of 300 feet is $5.<sup>00/100</sup> without plants &amp; for two adjoining<span class='line-break'> </span>of the same size $8.<sup>00/100</sup>, but, as we charged you only $3.<sup>50/100</sup> last year<span class='line-break'> </span>for the care of Lot #474 we shall not depart from the same charge<span class='line-break'> </span>for the care of it for [18]73 &amp; should you wish us to take care of<span class='line-break'> </span>both <a href='/pages/subjects/25007479' title='Lot 474'>lots viz #474</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007424' title='Lot 481'>&amp; #481</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/61127' title='Beech Avenue'>Beech Ave:</a> we shall take them on the </p>

<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>On Thursday<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-05-30'>May 30</date>, Decoration Day. you will<span class='line-break'> </span>admit only <u>Proprietors</u> with <u>vehicles</u>,<span class='line-break'> </span>and you will respect passes for<span class='line-break'> </span>vehicles issued by the "<a href='/pages/subjects/54945' title='Andrew, John Albion'>John A.<span class='line-break'> </span>Andrew</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007499' title='Grand Amy of the Republic'>Post" G.A.R.</a> to the extent<span class='line-break'> </span>of 30 (thirty) and no more. Please<span class='line-break'> </span>collect these passes &amp; return to me.<span class='line-break'> </span>Vehicles in the procession will be<span class='line-break'> </span>allowed to enter, also persons on<span class='line-break'> </span>foot without passes.</p>
<p>Respectfully Yrs.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-26'>May 26</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/74568' title='Fox, Joseph'>Joseph Fox Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I must respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>request you on Saturday afternoons &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>on the afternoons before all holidays,<span class='line-break'> </span>to place no cut grass or other refuse<span class='line-break'> </span>piles in the Avenues or Paths, as<span class='line-break'> </span>it is to late to remove them. I have no<span class='line-break'> </span>doubt you will see the propriety of<span class='line-break'> </span>such an order, and shall hope you<span class='line-break'> </span>will see that your men observe it.</p>
<p>Respectfully Yrs.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<h3><a name="page-1131996">CB03_0182</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='182'>182</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-26'>May 26 [187]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/105158' title='P. O&apos;Brian &amp; Co.'>OBrien &amp; Co</a></p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>I must respect<span class='line-break'></span>fully request you on Saturday after<span class='line-break'></span>noons and on the afternoons before all<span class='line-break'> </span>holidays, to place no cut grass or<span class='line-break'> </span>other refuse piles in the Avenues<span class='line-break'> </span>or Paths, as it is then to late to<span class='line-break'> </span>remove them. I have no doubt you<span class='line-break'> </span>will see the propriety of such a<span class='line-break'> </span>request &amp; shall hope you will<span class='line-break'> </span>direct your men to observe it.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn P.O.<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-05-27'>May 27 [18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee</a> Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm. on Grounds.</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/104995' title='Bucknam, John C.'>Mr Bucknam</a><span class='line-break'> </span>desires to remove two trees now on<span class='line-break'> </span>his tomb lot in <a href='/pages/subjects/59983' title='Hazel Dell'>Hazel Dell</a> &amp; to<span class='line-break'> </span>plant instead other &amp; better trees.</p>
<p>As he is now at work grading &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>sodding the lot, he would be very<span class='line-break'> </span>glad to have the matter decided now,<span class='line-break'> </span>so that he can remove the roots also.</p>
<p>The lots you mentioned to me this<span class='line-break'> </span>morning as being in poor order, are<span class='line-break'> </span><u>not</u> in care of the Corporation.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1131997">
<h3><a name="page-1131997">CB03_0183</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='183'>183</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-27'>May 27 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007505' title='Dexter, William S.'>W<sup>m</sup> S. Dexter</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>I understand from the <span class='line-break'> </span>late <a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>Sup<sup>t</sup> Col. Folsom</a> that you looked<span class='line-break'> </span>at some ground near the lot of<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25007506' title='Whitney, H. A.'>H.A. Whitney</a> Esq - with the view of buying<span class='line-break'> </span>a lot there.</p>
<p>The lot has been restaked so as to<span class='line-break'> </span>make a good lot of about 284 feet<span class='line-break'> </span>which I thought I would offer to you<span class='line-break'> </span>before any one else, as you had looked<span class='line-break'> </span>at it once.</p>
<p>I should be glad to have your decision<span class='line-break'> </span>before long, as I am having frequent<span class='line-break'> </span>applications for lots, but I shall not dis<span class='line-break'></span>pose of this before <date when='1873-06-07'>June 7<sup>th</sup></date> and hope to <span class='line-break'> </span>hear from you by that time</p>
<p>Respectfully <a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p><date when='1873-05-28'>May 28<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date><span class='line-break'> </span>Hon <a href='/pages/subjects/25007507' title='Bartlett, Sidney'>Sidney Bartlett</a>.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have the honor<span class='line-break'> </span>to acknowledge your favor of the 28<sup>th</sup> inst.<span class='line-break'> </span>I have had a statement made up,<span class='line-break'> </span>showing the details of the work done for<span class='line-break'> </span>you, adding also the amount of stone<span class='line-break'> </span>used in the foundation, which my clerk<span class='line-break'> </span>rendered in a separate bill, so that this<span class='line-break'> </span>account now comprises everything except<span class='line-break'> </span>the setting of the corner posts, which I think<span class='line-break'> </span>are not now ready.</p>
<p>I happened to meet <a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>Col. Folsom</a> and<span class='line-break'> </span>made some inquiries from him as to his<span class='line-break'> </span>agreement with you, and think you will<span class='line-break'> </span>find I have come within his estimate.</p>
<p>Respectfully Yrs. <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The piece for a lot<span class='line-break'> </span>similar in size &amp; position to <a href='/pages/subjects/67307' title='Lot 3549'>lot 3549</a><span class='line-break'> </span>would be $800.</p>
<p>We do not make it a habit to sell any<span class='line-break'> </span>lots but our own - but as this lot is in a<span class='line-break'> </span>prominent position, so that it is desirable<span class='line-break'> </span>to have it kept looking well, our trustee<span class='line-break'> </span>might possibly consent to disposing of it.<span class='line-break'> </span>At what price would sell it to us</p>
<p>Respectfully Yrs.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<h3><a name="page-1131999">CB03_0185</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='185'>185</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-05-29'>29<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p>[George?] B. [?] Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132000">CB03_0186</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">

<p>Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-05-30'>May 30, 1873.</date></p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The <a href='/pages/subjects/57656' title='Receiving Tomb'>Old Receiving<span class='line-break'> </span>Tomb</a> is very much crowded &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>I think provision for mine deposits<span class='line-break'> </span>is desirable.</p>
<p>I have this week examined the<span class='line-break'> </span>New Tomb and find that the roof<span class='line-break'> </span>to the vestibule leaks considerably &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>that the floor is not laid. These defects<span class='line-break'> </span>would not however prevent using<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>catacombs</a>, which I regret to<span class='line-break'> </span>find have been built too small,<span class='line-break'> </span>in width &amp; height.</p>
<p>If the Trustees would authorize<span class='line-break'> </span>the use of the New Tomb, when practi<span class='line-break'></span>cable, I think it would be an advantage.</p>
<p>Yrs respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-02'>June 2<sup>nd</sup> [187]3</date>.</p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007516' title='Macron, Mrs.'>Mrs Marcon</a></p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The Corporation will agree<span class='line-break'> </span>to put a new sod on your lot, thereby<span class='line-break'> </span>putting it in as good condition as before<span class='line-break'> </span>the damage occurred, at their expense.</p>
<p>If you wish to raise the lot at your<span class='line-break'> </span>expense we can raise it a foot for<span class='line-break'> </span>[$25?] or $30, and then sod it.</p>
<p>Hoping this may be satisfactory</p>
<p>I am respectfully yrs<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132005">CB03_0191</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth2' depth='2' title='=191'>=191</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-06-09'>June 9. 1873</date>.</p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you two plans of lots which<span class='line-break'> </span>belong to parties who wish to divide them differently, and<span class='line-break'> </span>exchange their present deeds.</p>
<p><u>First Case.</u><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25007529' title='Sherbourne, Warren'>Warren Sherbourne</a>, (<a href='/pages/subjects/25007530' title='Lot 3021'>Lots 3021</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007531' title='Lot 3022'>&amp; 3022.</a> 300 feet each.)<span class='line-break'> </span>States his lots are divided lengthwise, and that he wishes<span class='line-break'> </span>to divide them according to red numbers on plan, so as<span class='line-break'> </span>to deed away <u>new</u> <a href='/pages/subjects/25007531' title='Lot 3022'>lot 3022</a> on <a href='/pages/subjects/61256' title='Petunia Path'>Petunia Path</a>. His lot<span class='line-break'> </span>is measured to outside of posts, and within these are<span class='line-break'> </span>553 &amp; 296 feet = 849 feet or 89 feet <u>more</u> than his deeds give<span class='line-break'> </span>him. Should the Committee allow this change, I would<span class='line-break'> </span>respectfully suggest that this additional space of 89 feet be<span class='line-break'> </span>put between the two new lots as a passageway.</p>
<p><u>Second Case.</u><span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25007376' title='Whitcomb, Willaim W.'>W<sup>m</sup> W. Whitcomb</a> owner of <a href='/pages/subjects/25007477' title='Lot 3116'>3116 (230 ft.)</a> has<span class='line-break'> </span>bought <a href='/pages/subjects/25007478' title='lot 2031'>lot 2031</a> (300 ft.) and by permission of <a href='/pages/subjects/52528' title='Folsom, Charles W.'>late Supt. <!--C.W.F.--></a><span class='line-break'> </span>has united both lots in one for which he wishes to have<span class='line-break'> </span>a new deed, in place of the two deeds he now holds. You<span class='line-break'> </span>will notice he has enclosed 6 feet less than he is entitled to.</p>
<p>At the junction of <a href='/pages/subjects/58081' title='Halcyon Avenue'>Halcyon<!--A--></a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/58083' title='Ash Avenue'>Ash<!--A--></a> &amp; <a href='/pages/subjects/58082' title='Sycamore Avenue'>Sycamore Ave.</a><span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132006">CB03_0192</a></h3>

<p>is a small piece of land marked as Temporary Orna<span class='line-break'></span>mental Ground on my sale plans, but which has never<span class='line-break'> </span>been set aside for that purpose by the Comm. on Grounds.<span class='line-break'> </span>I enclose a tracing of it showing how I can divide it if<span class='line-break'> </span>the Committee do not object. <a href='/pages/subjects/25007532' title='Butler, G. S., Mr.'>Mr G. S. Butler</a> of <a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a><span class='line-break'> </span>is thinking of purchasing the 400 foot lot, if the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>can be decided on soon.</p>
<p>In regard to the "New Map" I have received an<span class='line-break'> </span>estimate from Shed &amp; Sawyer of the cost of placing on the<span class='line-break'> </span>present lithographs all the lots sold, and new paths &amp;c. which<span class='line-break'> </span>would be necessary in the first place, as we have no exact<span class='line-break'> </span>map on that scale, to alter the stone by.</p>
<p>I have seen the <a href='/pages/subjects/66038' title='Longfellow, Henry Wadsworth'>Lithographer Mr. Longfellow</a>, who<span class='line-break'> </span>has given me an estimate for altering the stone &amp; also<span class='line-break'> </span>for printing &amp; paper. <h3><a name="page-1132007">CB03_0193</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='193'>193</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn P.O<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-06-09'>June 9. 1873.</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>John T. Bradlee</a> Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find two of the [?] and<span class='line-break'> </span>the railing all so unsound that it will not pay<span class='line-break'> </span>to replace.</p>
<p>I estimate cost of replacing [?], planking and<span class='line-break'> </span>putting a railing of this pattern on at $115.00<span class='line-break'> </span>[diagram: sideview of bridge] This form of railing is not so expensive as that<span class='line-break'> </span>now on the bridge, and is certainly as useful.</p>
<p>The cost of an <a href='/pages/subjects/25007379' title='Auburn Lake Bride'>iron bridge</a> I estimate as follows<span class='line-break'> </span>4 Iron Beams of I section with a wooden flooring<span class='line-break'> </span>3 inches thick, width of bridge 15 feet and with a<span class='line-break'> </span>railing consisting of two (2) posts on each side<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>and 3 bars across [diagram: sideview of steel bridge]</th> <th>$225<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>The bars are simply round from tube, painted</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>the posts are of <u>neat</u> &amp; <u>simple</u> design, about 4 inches</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>diam. at bottom and less at top.</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>Cost of changes in masonry, repairing road &amp;c.</td> <td>50.</td> </tr> <tr><td>If, in addition to the railing across the bridge</td> <td>$275</td> </tr> <tr><td>it is desirable to continue the railing five or</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>six feet beyond the bridge as each end, as in the</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>old one, the cost will be increased</td> <td>75.</td> </tr> <tr><td>Total cost - estimated at</td> <td>$350</td> </tr> </tbody> </table></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1132008">
<h3><a name="page-1132008">CB03_0194</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='194'>194</span></p>
<p>This is the cheapest <a href='/pages/subjects/25007379' title='Auburn Lake Bride'>iron bridge</a> which we could put up,<span class='line-break'> </span>and I think as the repairs to the old one cost so much,<span class='line-break'> </span>will prove cheapest in the end.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-10'>June 10 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007535' title='Chickering, George H.'>Geo H. Chickering</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dr Sir,</p>
<p>I examined your tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>today &amp; find that before we can put in<span class='line-break'> </span>the <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>catacombs</a> we must remove the arch, so<span class='line-break'> </span>that the work amounts to removing the<span class='line-break'> </span>present tomb and putting in a new one.</p>
<p>We are not in the habit of procurring<span class='line-break'> </span>marble or any kind of "finished stone" as<span class='line-break'> </span>the By Laws of the Corporation do no per<span class='line-break'></span>mit the Sup<sup>t</sup> to do this.</p>
<p>I cannot therefore give you as reliable an<span class='line-break'> </span>estimate, but I judge that the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>sixteen <a href='/pages/subjects/66005' title='Catacomb Tombs'>catacombs</a>, with slate shelves &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>marble fronts and an improved en<span class='line-break'></span>trance would amount to at least $3000.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132009">
<h3><a name="page-1132009">CB03_0195</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='195'>195</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-11'>June 11<sup>th</sup></date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/54731' title='Batchelder, Samuel, Jr.'>Sam<sup>l</sup> Batchelder Jr.</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sec'y</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Dr Char. D Honsa<span class='line-break'> </span>lot was estimated last August for Perpe<span class='line-break'></span>Care (G) at $375. He is now prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>to act and would be glad to know<span class='line-break'> </span>if there is any reason for not taking his<span class='line-break'> </span>lot at the same valuation.</p>
<p>I have been to the lot, and should<span class='line-break'> </span>consider there was none, as the lot is<span class='line-break'> </span>in good order and there is no fence or<span class='line-break'> </span>curb &amp; but two very simple headstones.</p>
<p>If the committe prefer I can send a<span class='line-break'> </span>new report, but as he is in some hurry &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>we have a number on hand, I thought<span class='line-break'> </span>the past might answer.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering</a></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-11'>June 11<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007543' title='Bayley, James R.'>Jas R. Bayley</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>

Folsom</a> &amp; has been ready for payment<span class='line-break'> </span>since<date when='1872-01'> Jan'y 1872</date>.</p>

<div id="page-1132020">
<h3><a name="page-1132020">CB03_0206</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='206'>206</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-28'>June 28<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25007378' title='Hastings, Walter'>Walter Hastings</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I called at your<span class='line-break'> </span>office today but did not find you.<span class='line-break'> </span>The posts are being set, the delay<span class='line-break'> </span>having been, in waiting for our<span class='line-break'> </span>surveyor to stake the right points.</p>
<p>I can find no charge against<span class='line-break'> </span>you for any tulip trees - only<span class='line-break'> </span>for some magnolias - It has been<span class='line-break'> </span>too dry this spring to do anything<span class='line-break'> </span>about them, &amp; therefore I have<span class='line-break'> </span>been waiting till I happen to <span class='line-break'> </span>see you again.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-28'>June 28<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/66038' title='Longfellow, Henry Wadsworth'>H.W. Longfellow</a> Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>We have made up<span class='line-break'> </span>our minds to make the alterations on<span class='line-break'> </span>the stone formerly used &amp; have some<span class='line-break'> </span>copies struck off if it can be done<span class='line-break'> </span>at about your figures to me. Will you<span class='line-break'> </span>therefore please see the stone report.</p>
<p>I understand it is at the City Hall<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/52559' title='Boston, MA'>Boston</a>, and by requiring at our<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston Office 16 Pemberton Sq. either<span class='line-break'> </span>the Sec<sup>y</sup> or Treas<sup>r</sup> will give you any<span class='line-break'> </span>information regarding it which they<span class='line-break'> </span>can. I would like to hear from you<span class='line-break'> </span>soon, as we are prepared &amp; desirous<span class='line-break'> </span>to go ahead if the stone will answer.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></a></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>I have been expecting<span class='line-break'> </span>to hear your price on the coal &amp; should<span class='line-break'> </span>be glad to know, as I am now prepared<span class='line-break'> </span>to buy the following amt.<span class='line-break'> </span>For Mt. Auburn Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>18 tons Furnace Coal delivered in Yard<span class='line-break'> </span>of <a href='/pages/subjects/102074' title='Engine house'>Engine House</a>, 45 tons Furnace Coal<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered in cellars of <a href='/pages/subjects/61312' title='Greenhouse'>Greenhouses</a> or<span class='line-break'> </span>in <a href='/pages/subjects/61312' title='Greenhouse'>Greenhouse</a> Yard, and 10 tons<span class='line-break'> </span>stove coal at <a href='/pages/subjects/25008827' title='Superintendent Office'>Superintendent Office</a>.</p>
<p>In addition I will buy for myself<span class='line-break'> </span>12 tons furnace coal &amp; 6 tons range coal<span class='line-break'> </span>delivered in the cellar of house. This <span class='line-break'> </span>will have to be carried in a short distance as<span class='line-break'> </span>bins by windows are full.</p>
<p>Yrs truly <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></a></p>
<p><date when='1873-06-30'>June 30<sup>th</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/105069' title='Shedd &amp; Sawyer'>Shed &amp; Sawyer</a></p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>

I should like to have<span class='line-break'> </span>the height taken on pegs occasionally as<span class='line-break'> </span>it will probably be desirable to make<span class='line-break'> </span>some future [attealing?]</p>
<p>Please send us bill for same<span class='line-break'> </span>in a day or two.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p>He tells me he can make the<span class='line-break'> </span>alterations as proposed on the<span class='line-break'> </span>old stone and then take an impres<span class='line-break'></span>sion on the new stone and print<span class='line-break'> </span>from that -</p>
<p>In this way he says he can give<span class='line-break'> </span>good impressions, and at the<span class='line-break'> </span>same time we shall not be obliged<span class='line-break'> </span>to buy a new stone.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132023">CB03_0209</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='209'>209</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-07-07'>July 7. [18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/52526' title='Bradlee, John T.'>J.T. Bradlee Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find that <span class='line-break'> </span>in order to supply all necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>signs on avenues &amp; paths, we<span class='line-break'> </span>need 56 <u>iron</u> signs or 10 more<span class='line-break'> </span>(total 66) if the paths are to be<span class='line-break'> </span>laid out over the piece of land<span class='line-break'> </span>East of the <a href='/pages/subjects/61326' title='Well House Gazebo'>well house</a>, which<span class='line-break'> </span>was ploughed last spring. I also<span class='line-break'> </span>find 28 wooden signs wanting - <span class='line-break'> </span>that is, if these signs are to be<span class='line-break'> </span>replaced in same condition as<span class='line-break'> </span>they were originally. If in iron, which<span class='line-break'> </span>certainly looks better, the total no.<span class='line-break'> </span>required would be 94. I have<span class='line-break'> </span>written to the firm who made them<span class='line-break'> </span>before for a price, but have rec'd no<span class='line-break'> </span>answer yet.</p>
<p>Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a></p>
<p>Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-07-08'>July 8. [18]73</date></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132024">CB03_0210</a></h3>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='210'>210</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span><date when='1873-07-08'>July 8. [18]73</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/95125' title='Snow, Samuel T.'>S.T. Snow Esq</a></p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>I went this<span class='line-break'> </span>morning to <a href='/pages/subjects/80045' title='Wetherell, John G.'>Mr Wetherell's</a> <a href='/pages/subjects/64043' title='Lot 1170'>Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>1170</a> and find that the sod tho'<span class='line-break'> </span>dry in a few spots, looks better<span class='line-break'> </span>than the average of the lots this<span class='line-break'> </span>dry weather. I also find by my<span class='line-break'> </span>daily reports that the lot has<span class='line-break'> </span>been put in order <u>four</u> <u>times</u><span class='line-break'> </span>since <date when='1873-05-01'>May 1<sup>st</sup></date> beside watering it<span class='line-break'> </span>somewhat. The lot is a 400 ft lot<span class='line-break'> </span>and we have been getting only<span class='line-break'> </span>$5.00 for annual care. The regular<span class='line-break'> </span>charge for a 300 ft lot, and I can<span class='line-break'> </span>not see any reasonable cause for<span class='line-break'> </span>complaint.</p>
<p>I have made inquiries, but have<span class='line-break'> </span>been unable to find out what<span class='line-break'> </span>was requested by <a href='/pages/subjects/80045' title='Wetherell, John G.'>Mr Wetherall.</a></p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The only safe which<span class='line-break'> </span>we have at the Cemetery is too small to con<span class='line-break'></span>tain more than the Interment Records and the<span class='line-break'> </span>cash book &amp; cash of the Gatekeeper.</p>
<p>It seems to me that the orders &amp; books con<span class='line-break'></span>nected with the annual care of lots &amp; the<span class='line-break'> </span>labor &amp; materials department, are too valuable<span class='line-break'> </span>to be left entirely unprotected at night &amp; during<span class='line-break'> </span>Sundays, especially as the Superintendent's office is<span class='line-break'> </span>in a wooden building, and want of room at<span class='line-break'> </span>the gate as well as convenience, require that it<span class='line-break'> </span>should remain so.</p>
<p>I can get along without the safe, with out any<span class='line-break'> </span>inconvenience, if the trustees feel disposed to<span class='line-break'> </span>run the risk, whatever it may be.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132030">CB03_0216</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='216'>216</span></p>
<p><u>Return</u> this <u>order</u> to the <u>Supt.</u> when <u>finished</u> and <u>notify<span class='line-break'> </span>him before sending bill.</u></p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>[diagram: triangular lot with plots 1,2,3 marked]</p>
<p>In <a href='/pages/subjects/25008927' title='Lot 2328'>Lot 2328</a>, on <a href='/pages/subjects/61271' title='Rosemary Path'>Rosemary Path</a> plan<span class='line-break'> </span>build the following as per plan - Build 3 brick graves for<span class='line-break'> </span>enough back from front fence to allow gate to open - Remove<span class='line-break'> </span>into No.2 the body in Grave now covered with Myrtle, preserving<span class='line-break'> </span>Myrtle &amp; replanting it if possible - Remove into No.1 the body in<span class='line-break'> </span>Grave (A) in corner placing remains in new box - Leave No.3 vacant<span class='line-break'> </span>Use same sod if possible - If lot is wide enough for 4 brick graves<span class='line-break'> </span>in a row, remove C to 4th brick grave between No.1 and fence. If<span class='line-break'> </span>not, remove the body to point of lot without making a brick grave,<span class='line-break'> </span>put it in a box if desirable - Build 2 foundations at Nos.<span class='line-break'> </span>1 &amp; 2, 2'4" long x 1'2" wide this work is to be done just as soon<span class='line-break'> </span>as sods can be replaced without injury.<span class='line-break'> </span>Leave grade of sod below the fence.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W. Lovering</a> Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25006742' title='A. C., per'>P.A.C.</a></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132032">CB03_0218</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='218'>218</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-07-23'>July 23<sup>rd</sup> [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/25008974' title='Payson, Samuel R.'>S.R. Payson</a> Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>We have an order<span class='line-break'> </span>on our books to "Grade &amp; Sod a lot"<span class='line-break'> </span>which you have purchased recently.</p>
<p>I learn that you are thinking<span class='line-break'> </span>of building a tomb, &amp; therefore,<span class='line-break'> </span>would respectfully uniform you<span class='line-break'> </span>that, unless you prefer otherwise,<span class='line-break'> </span>it would be best to defer doing<span class='line-break'> </span>anything to the lot, until the tomb<span class='line-break'> </span>is finished.</p>
<p>I shall be glad to do whatever<span class='line-break'> </span>work you may wish done on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot or tomb</p>
<p>Respectfully Yrs.<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a></p>
<p><date when='1873-07-23'>July 23 [187]3</date></p>
<p><a href='/pages/subjects/93771' title='Deblois, Stephen G.'>S.G. Deblois Esq.</a></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>We have completed the<span class='line-break'> </span>alterations on <a href='/pages/subjects/25007546' title='Trinity Church Lot'>Trinity Church Lot</a> &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>also sodded it. The numbers I have<span class='line-break'> </span>been delayed about, but hope to<span class='line-break'> </span>get them cut soon.</p>
<p>Our By-laws require that every<span class='line-break'> </span>lot shall be fenced, or marked by<span class='line-break'> </span>boundary posts, and I shall be glad<span class='line-break'> </span>if you will authorize me to have<span class='line-break'> </span>boundary posts set. I have only <span class='line-break'> </span>square &amp; octagonal topped posts.<span class='line-break'> </span>Should you wish to put up something<span class='line-break'> </span>more elaborate by the future, I will<span class='line-break'> </span>take the posts back &amp; allow you something<span class='line-break'> </span>for them.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1132039">CB03_0225</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='225'>225</span></p>
<p><date when='873-08-04'>Aug 4 [187]3</date></p>
<p>[S.W. Easty?] Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>It seems probable that the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>will makes no objection to <a href='/pages/subjects/25008996' title='Stogg, Mr.'>Mr Stogg's</a> using the<span class='line-break'> </span>ornamental lawn in rear of his lot for interment<span class='line-break'> </span>purposes by his paying for the difference in price<span class='line-break'> </span>between land need for onramental &amp; interment purposes</p>
<p>Therefore <a href='/pages/subjects/25008996' title='Stogg, Mr.'>Mr Stogg</a> can erect a tomb on the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot. It is necessary that his design be approved<span class='line-break'> </span>by the trustedes &amp; that he obtain a tomb right.</p>
<p>Experience, therefore your plans are sufficiently<span class='line-break'> </span>far advanced. I shall be happy to lay them<span class='line-break'> </span>before the trustees and the question of land care<span class='line-break'> </span>be settled at same time.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a> Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='237'>237</span></p>
<p><date when='1873-08-08'>Aug 8 [187]3</date></p>
<p>Messrs <a href='/pages/subjects/25009043' title='Burnham &amp; Lowell'>Burnham &amp; Lowell</a></p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>
<p>Please make<span class='line-break'> </span>what repairs are necessary on fence<span class='line-break'> </span>on <a href='/pages/subjects/25009044' title='Lot 1518'>Lot 1518</a>, <a href='/pages/subjects/61187' title='Geranium Path'>Geranium Path</a>, front<span class='line-break'> </span>being broken in cutting a tree.</p>
<p>When you are out please look<span class='line-break'> </span>at the signs "under the perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Corporation" which are fastened<span class='line-break'> </span>to the iron fences, and see if they<span class='line-break'> </span>can be neatly altered to stand in<span class='line-break'> </span>the ground as on many of the lots<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; let me know the cost apiece for<span class='line-break'> </span>altering say 50.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>J.W.Lovering</a><span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p><date when='1873-08-08'>August 8 [187]3</date></p>

<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The iron fence<span class='line-break'> </span>which surrounds your <a href='/pages/subjects/25009046' title='Lot 2606'>Lot (#2606)</a> is<span class='line-break'> </span>broken if you would like to have it<span class='line-break'> </span>repaired please advise us and we <span class='line-break'> </span>will see that it is promptly done and<span class='line-break'> </span>at as little expense as possible.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/58078' title='Lovering, James W.'>James W.Lovering</a> Supt<span class='line-break'> </span><a href='/pages/subjects/25006742' title='A. C., per'>P.A.C.</a></p>

<p>I believe I am correct<span class='line-break'> </span>in supposing you intended to have your<span class='line-break'> </span>tomb plastered, please let me know<span class='line-break'> </span>by return mail, if possible, if I am<span class='line-break'> </span>right, as we are about ready to com<span class='line-break'></span>mence.</p>

<div id="page-1132055">
<h3><a name="page-1132055">CB03_0241</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='241'>241</span></p>
<p>Mt Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Aug 11. 1873</p>
<p>J.T. Bradlee Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I saw the <span class='line-break'> </span>Agent in regard to the insurance<span class='line-break'> </span>and the old policy has been<span class='line-break'> </span>extended to Aug 18<sup>th</sup> noon.</p>
<p>Your memo. was House $1000, Barn &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>shed $700, carts wagons $500, Hay $200<span class='line-break'> </span>Horses $1200, total $3600. -</p>
<p>Agent says the company will<span class='line-break'> </span>not take but <u>$1500</u> on <u>any one</u> barn<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; property in it, but if you will put<span class='line-break'> </span>$1000 more on house, he can take<span class='line-break'> </span>out a policy in another company &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>make up the amount on barn, all<span class='line-break'> </span>this at old rates.</p>
<p>Respectfully. <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Aug 12 [187]3</p>
<p>Messrs G.H. [Mizeley?] &amp; Co</p>
<p>Dear Sirs</p>
<p>Your favor of<span class='line-break'> </span>Aug 9<sup>th</sup> rec'd. Please deliver all<span class='line-break'> </span>you can before Sept 1<sup>st</sup> and the<span class='line-break'> </span>balance as early in Sept. as<span class='line-break'> </span>possible. Please send us a bill<span class='line-break'> </span>the 1<sup>st</sup> of Sept. for all delivered<span class='line-break'> </span>in August.</p>
<p>Please ask your teamsters to<span class='line-break'> </span>hand the manure ^<sup>tickets</sup> to the Engineer<span class='line-break'> </span>at the Engine house near the East<span class='line-break'> </span>Gate. Our Gardener Mr Joseph Collins<span class='line-break'> </span>will inform you where to deliver.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1132056">
<h3><a name="page-1132056">CB03_0242</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='242'>242</span></p>
<p>Aug 12<sup>t</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>Jonathan Mann Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your valued favor of<span class='line-break'> </span>Aug 7<sup>th</sup> at hand. We will build the tombs<span class='line-break'> </span>and grade &amp; sod the lots, 4272 &amp; 4273 Palm Ave<span class='line-break'> </span>at the prices named in the enclosed orders,<span class='line-break'> </span>providing we do the whole of the work of excavating<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; building, or the whole of grading &amp; sodding, but we<span class='line-break'> </span>cannot afford to furnish the labor at these prices<span class='line-break'> </span>unless we take the whole of either of these portions of<span class='line-break'> </span>the work.</p>
<p>We will give you all the time of day &amp; gang<span class='line-break'> </span>which we can, but having already undertaken<span class='line-break'> </span>some other work where he will be needed, must<span class='line-break'> </span>reserve the right to use him for the best general good<span class='line-break'> </span>of the proprietors.</p>
<p>If this meets with your approval, please return<span class='line-break'> </span>these orders signed by the proprietors or by yourself<span class='line-break'> </span>as <u>agent</u> for them. The plan of the tomb must be approved<span class='line-break'> </span>by the committee on Lots.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1132057">CB03_0243</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='243'>243</span></p>
<p>4272 Palm</p>
<p>Jon<sup>n</sup> Mann Agt for Chas F. Leeds</p>
<p>Grade &amp; sod lot according to customary<span class='line-break'> </span>manner at this Cemetery at following prices<span class='line-break'> </span>Loam $1.00 pr load<span class='line-break'> </span>Manure $3.00 [per load]<span class='line-break'> </span>Sods 3 3/4<sup>c</sup> foot<span class='line-break'> </span>Labor $2.50 pr day</p>
<p>Payments on account of work done to <span class='line-break'> </span>be made monthly.</p>
<p>4273 Palm</p>
<p>Jon<sup>n</sup> Mann Agt for Miss Emma A. Leeds</p>
<p>Excavate for &amp; build tomb furnishing all<span class='line-break'> </span>material except cutstone &amp; marble fronts &amp; tiles<span class='line-break'> </span>according to customary manner at this Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>Material to be charged at 10% advance on<span class='line-break'> </span>cost to corporation, and when taken from store<span class='line-break'> </span>house cost of hauling ot the charged in addition.<span class='line-break'> </span>Labor of excavating &amp; common labor $2.<sup>50</sup> pr day<span class='line-break'> </span>horse &amp; team $4.00 pr day; mason's labor $3.00 pr<span class='line-break'> </span>day, use of derrick being counted as one<span class='line-break'> </span>man.</p>
<p>Payments on account of work done to <span class='line-break'> </span>be made monthly.</p>
<p>4273 Palm</p>
<p>Jon<sup>n</sup> Mann Agt for Miss Emma A. Leeds</p>
<p>Grade &amp; sod lot according to customary<span class='line-break'> </span>manner at this Cemetery at following prices<span class='line-break'> </span>Loam $1.00 pr load<span class='line-break'> </span>Manure 3.00 pr load<span class='line-break'> </span>Sods 3 3/4 cts pr foot<span class='line-break'> </span>Labor $2.50 pr day</p>
<p>Payment monthly on account of<span class='line-break'> </span>work done.</p>
<p>4272 Palm</p>
<p>Jon<sup>n</sup> Mann, Agt for Chas F. Leeds</p>
<p>Excavate^<sup>for</sup> &amp; build tomb, furnishing all<span class='line-break'> </span>material except cutstone &amp; marble fronts or tiles<span class='line-break'> </span>according to the customary manner at this Cemetery.<span class='line-break'> </span>Material to be charged at 10% advancement to<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, and when taken from storehouse cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of hauling to be charged in addition<span class='line-break'> </span>Labor of excavating &amp; common labor $2.<sup>50</sup> pr day, horse<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; team $4.00 pr day; mason's labor $3.00 pr day, use<span class='line-break'> </span>of derrick being counted as one man.</p>
<p>Payment on accoutn of work done<span class='line-break'> </span>to be made monthly.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132058">CB03_0244</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='244'>244</span></p>
<p>Aug 12<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Shall I refuse to have the<span class='line-break'> </span>curbings placed on the avenue or path line on<span class='line-break'> </span>any more lots, even when there is a complete<span class='line-break'> </span>curb around the lot also? Do you wish to<span class='line-break'> </span>apply this to the borders in front of tomb lots?<span class='line-break'> </span>On all the tombs lately built the borders have<span class='line-break'> </span>been enclosed tho' the land has not been purchased.</p>
<p>I will be obliged if you will give me<span class='line-break'> </span>explicit directions in this matter at your<span class='line-break'> </span>early convenience.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<p>August 12 [187]3</p>
<p>Mrs. Dexter Roby</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The interest upon the<span class='line-break'> </span>sum deposited will not be more than<span class='line-break'> </span>sufficient for the ordinary care of your<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot as taken by the Corporation. Under<span class='line-break'> </span>these circumstances if you wish us to<span class='line-break'> </span>put in the three Myrtle graves at your<span class='line-break'> </span>expense, we will do so at once upon<span class='line-break'> </span>the receipt of enclosed order, signed.</p>

<p>August 12 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr. E.F. Young</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>You will allow no teams<span class='line-break'> </span>to pass through the gate either to deliver or<span class='line-break'> </span>take away materials, except those belong<span class='line-break'></span>ing to the Cemetery, those working under a<span class='line-break'> </span>general permit, and those delivering materi<span class='line-break'></span>al for the Corporation. I wish you to hold<span class='line-break'> </span>youself personally responsible for the proper<span class='line-break'> </span>enforcement of the above order.</p>

<div id="page-1132062">
<h3><a name="page-1132062">CB03_0248</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='248'>248</span></p>
<p>Mount Auburn Aug 13 /73</p>
<p>John T. Bradlee Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest. &amp;c.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I enclose you a sketch of<span class='line-break'> </span>proposed path &amp; new lots in rear of Mrs Merrill's<span class='line-break'> </span>lot on Lime Avenue, which I think will leave as<span class='line-break'> </span>little waste land as any which will allow the ground<span class='line-break'> </span>to be divided into good shapes lots.</p>
<p>I would suggest that Mrs Merrill l be asked to<span class='line-break'> </span>purchase the 660 ft enclosed in purple dotted lines, in<span class='line-break'> </span>the rear of her lot 2667, as ornamental ground. (she now<span class='line-break'> </span>owns the piece marked O.G. on plan)</p>
<p>On this piece of 660 ft would be room for a small<span class='line-break'> </span>fountain, and the balance could be laid out with<span class='line-break'> </span>shrubs or flowers. If she would also purchase the piece<span class='line-break'> </span>opposit 387 feet (about) as ornamental land it would<span class='line-break'> </span>greatly improve the remaining lots which would contain<span class='line-break'> </span>about 2861 feet.</p>
<p>I also enclose sketch of proposed paths on land<span class='line-break'> </span>East of the Well house, being the same now on the litho<span class='line-break'></span>graphed plan. I cannot find any record of this acceptance<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Trustees.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1132064">CB03_0250</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='250'>250</span></p>
<p>Aug 15<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>Jonathan Mann Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Agent for owners of Lots 4272 &amp; 4273</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of Aug 14<sup>th</sup> at Land. The<span class='line-break'> </span>Committee on Lots (of the Trustees) have notified me<span class='line-break'> </span>that no tomb must be built, until the plan has been<span class='line-break'> </span>approved by them, so that the sooner you can make it con<span class='line-break'></span>venient to submit your plan, the sooner this matter can<span class='line-break'> </span>be settled.</p>
<p>Mr Sam<sup>l</sup> Batchelder can furnish you with a permit<span class='line-break'> </span>for laborers &amp; teams, a separate permit being required for each lot. If<span class='line-break'> </span>you wish a General permit, it would be necessary to apply to the Trustees.</p>
<p>If you have bought your brick, cement &amp; covers, I<span class='line-break'> </span>prefer you should furnish them. I will furnish all<span class='line-break'> </span>other materials usually furnished have at 10% advance<span class='line-break'> </span>on cost to us, hauling to be charged extra if necessary,<span class='line-break'> </span>except that I shall charge $2.00 pr load for sand for mortar<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; 12 1/2<sup>cents</sup> pr ft for lead. I will furnish common labor at <span class='line-break'> </span>2 &amp; 2 1/2, mason's labor @ $3.<sup>25</sup> pr day (counting derrick<span class='line-break'> </span>as a man) a leader @ $3.50 pr day, horse &amp; team $4.00 pr day</p>
<p>I will grade &amp; sod @ $2.62 1/2 pr day, furnishing</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132065">
<h3><a name="page-1132065">CB03_0251</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='251'>251</span></p>
<p>loam @ $1.00 pr load sods 3 1/4<sup>cents</sup> pr foot, manure $3.00 pr load<span class='line-break'> </span>gravel 50<sup>cents</sup> pr load, doing the work in the manner<span class='line-break'> </span>customary here, payments to be made monthly on<span class='line-break'> </span>account of works.</p>
<p>If you give us all the work mentioned above<span class='line-break'> </span>that is, the furnishing of all supplies except the brick<span class='line-break'> </span>cement &amp; covers, which we are prepared to furnish<span class='line-break'> </span>I will deduct from your final bill, 25<sup>cents</sup> for each<span class='line-break'> </span>day of mason's labor, and 12 1/2<sup>cents</sup> pr day for common<span class='line-break'> </span>labor &amp; grading &amp; sodding.</p>
<p>I will give you all the time of Day &amp; gang<span class='line-break'> </span>which I conveniently can.</p>
<p>These prices I am sure will average favorably<span class='line-break'> </span>without outside prices and the advance on the cost<span class='line-break'> </span>of labor no more than a fair one. I can of course<span class='line-break'> </span>do a large job, much cheaper than a small one.</p>
<p>I regrect to call your attention to the fact that<span class='line-break'> </span>your teamster in delivering brick on Wednesday last<span class='line-break'> </span>damaged the fence on Lot 2412 considerably. Will you<span class='line-break'> </span>undertake to put it in order or should I have it<span class='line-break'> </span>done at your expense?</p>
<p>Hoping that the above will meet your views<span class='line-break'> </span>in regard to prices, I am respectfully</p>
<p>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1132073">CB03_0259</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='259'>259</span></p>
<p>Aug 19 [187]3</p>
<p>Messes G.H. Mesely &amp; Co.</p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>
<p>I regret to be obliged to<span class='line-break'> </span>call your attention to the measurement of the<span class='line-break'> </span>manure; I cannot make the tickets agree with<span class='line-break'> </span>the amount delivered within 25% !! even <span class='line-break'> </span>when we measure the manure piled as high<span class='line-break'> </span>in the carts are your own teamsters state it was.<span class='line-break'> </span>and I can't quite see how the carts can hold<span class='line-break'> </span>as much, even when heaped up.</p>
<p>I wish you would have the matter looked<span class='line-break'> </span>up &amp; made right <u>before you deliver us any more</u><span class='line-break'> </span>for I am satisfied we are not getting what<span class='line-break'> </span>we should, if we pay for what the tickets call for.</p>
<p>I am ready to pay for every inch we get but<span class='line-break'> </span>I am not willing to pay for any more. Please give<span class='line-break'> </span>this attention as soon as you can and oblige</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<p>August 19 [187]3</p>
<p>Jona. Mann Esq.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Your favor of 16 th. inst.<span class='line-break'> </span>is recd. I cannot authorize you to work<span class='line-break'> </span>on the Tombs on Lots 4272 &amp; 4273, or to bring<span class='line-break'> </span>in materials for them until you obtain a<span class='line-break'> </span>special permit and file it here. When<span class='line-break'> </span>you obtain this you will be at liberty to do<span class='line-break'> </span>such work yourself as is in accordance with<span class='line-break'> </span>the general regulations of the Cemetery and<span class='line-break'> </span>the special contract for building the tombs<span class='line-break'> </span>and furnishing the lots, which we have made<span class='line-break'> </span>with you.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>J.E.C.</p>
<p>August 19 [187]3.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132084">CB03_0270</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='270'>270</span></p>
<p>August 26 [187]3.</p>
<p>Ms. Abby L. Faulkner<span class='line-break'> </span>West Roxbury</p>
<p>Dear Madam,</p>
<p>In placing Lots<span class='line-break'> </span>under the perpetual care of the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>provision is made only for what is then in <span class='line-break'> </span>the Lot, and the placing of Monuments, Myr<span class='line-break'></span>tle Graves, and improvements of this kind <span class='line-break'> </span>on the ground greatly increases the cost of <span class='line-break'> </span>care to the Corporation. Under these cir<span class='line-break'></span>cumstances, before you make any change, <span class='line-break'> </span>I would like to have you write me fully <span class='line-break'> </span>as to what you desire. The Corporation <span class='line-break'> </span>wish to afford every chance to Proprietors <span class='line-break'> </span>to beautify their Lots, but you will readily <span class='line-break'> </span>see that if the income of the deposit is<span class='line-break'> </span>only sufficient to keep the lot in its<span class='line-break'> </span>original repair it will not suffice to<span class='line-break'> </span>keep up any improvements.</p>
<p>Very respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>J.E.C.</p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Sept 5 [187]3</p>
<p>James M. Perkins Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>130 State St. Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of 3d.<span class='line-break'> </span>inst. enclosing order for Top dressing your<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot @ $3.00 is recd. We do not think<span class='line-break'> </span>we can afford to do this at a less<span class='line-break'> </span>price than $4.00 as the price we charge <span class='line-break'> </span>is only sufficient to cover the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>labor and material. Also, as other parties<span class='line-break'> </span>are paying $4.00 for lots of the same size<span class='line-break'> </span>as yours, we do not think it would be<span class='line-break'> </span>just to do your work at a less price<span class='line-break'> </span>than they pay.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>J.E.C.</p>

<p>[Diagrams: Greenhouse No. 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 and proposed No. 6]</p>
<p>[Diagram: No 4 &amp; 5 with note: Cast iron Pipes out &amp; return on each side of No 4 &amp; 5]</p>

<div id="page-1132102">
<h3><a name="page-1132102">CB03_0289</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='289'>289</span></p>
<p>Sept 29 [18]73</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>On reexamining my estimate, I find that accidentaly, I ommitted<span class='line-break'> </span>to allow any percentage for contingencies, the $1050 just covering the expenses<span class='line-break'> </span>I think it would be safer to ask for the appropriation of $1200 to cover all<span class='line-break'> </span>Respectfully J.W. Lovering -</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn Sept 9 [18]73</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I estimate the cost of completing<span class='line-break'> </span>the new greenhouse at $1050 (one thousand &amp; fifty dollars)<span class='line-break'> </span>This provides for connecting the pipes which all to heat<span class='line-break'> </span>it with the furnace in the work room which now heats<span class='line-break'> </span>No 4 and No 5, and which would probably prove<span class='line-break'> </span>powerful enough except in the coldest weather, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>even then it may do.</p>
<p>Should it be found insufficient, I would suggest<span class='line-break'> </span>that a small furnace be placed near the present are<span class='line-break'> </span>in the workshop, the pipes of both to connect with all<span class='line-break'> </span>three houses, so that either furnace could be used alone<span class='line-break'> </span>or both could be used in severe weather.</p>
<p>House No 3 is now heated by a furnace in the<span class='line-break'> </span>corner next Mt. Auburn St. The house is rather lightly<span class='line-break'> </span>built &amp; may want some extensive repairs before very<span class='line-break'> </span>long - I would suggest that it might be desirable to<span class='line-break'> </span>dipense with the furnace in No 3 <u>altogether</u>, and<span class='line-break'> </span>connect it by pipes with the furnaces in the workshop - <span class='line-break'> </span>my idea being that it is most economical both in<span class='line-break'> </span>labor &amp; fuel to have as few fires as possible.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>(sketch enclosed)<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
