<div id="page-1132109">
<h3><a name="page-1132109">CB03_0296</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='296'>296</span></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Sept 10, 1873</p>
<p>John T. Bradlee Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Prest.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you plans &amp; papers relating<span class='line-break'> </span>to the Stone Farm received last April, and with<span class='line-break'> </span>them a new plan modified somewhat from Col. Folsom's<span class='line-break'> </span>plan, after a careful examination of the ground &amp; maps.</p>
<p>The principal differences consist in some changes<span class='line-break'> </span>in location of <u>Avenues</u>, which, without injuring the<span class='line-break'> </span>grades of the avenues or increasing the expense in<span class='line-break'> </span>building, leave the land in better shape for division<span class='line-break'> </span>into regular lots; and in Ornamental Grounds (shown<span class='line-break'> </span>on plan in green) in dispensing with a lake at <u>b</u><span class='line-break'> </span>as I think it would be difficult to provide water<span class='line-break'> </span>for it, and in adding some land around the<span class='line-break'> </span>well house.</p>
<p>The drainage of that portion of land between Eagle<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenue &amp; J. Stone's land (except a small piece near<span class='line-break'> </span>St Paul's Lot which drains into a pond near there)<span class='line-break'> </span>is along the avenues toward the proposed <u>entrance</u>,<span class='line-break'> </span>distant from Charles River but 5 or 600 ft.</p>
<p>The drainage of the portion between Eagle Ave &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Coolidge Avenue is provided for over the avenues and by<span class='line-break'> </span>a short drain &amp; via Falcon Ave. to the drain now emptying<span class='line-break'> </span>into Charles River in case cesspools are not sufficient</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132110">
<h3><a name="page-1132110">CB03_0297</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='297'>297</span></p>
<p>I should suggest that the Avenues &amp; Ornamental Lands<span class='line-break'> </span>be graded first at a cost of $2500 finished, except<span class='line-break'> </span>that this makes no provision for gutters either paved or<span class='line-break'> </span>Cemented.</p>
<p>After the avenues are finished, several parts of the <span class='line-break'> </span>ground will not require very much labor &amp; could be<span class='line-break'> </span>made ready for sale quite easily, and the cost could<span class='line-break'> </span>be more readily &amp; satisfactorily estimated.</p>
<p>The heaviest piece of work in preparing the land<span class='line-break'> </span>for sale, is the filling of the hollow about opposite to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Winchester estate. This will require some 7000 yards<span class='line-break'> </span>of filling and I do not see how this quantity can be<span class='line-break'> </span>made any less by any plan of laying out the ground.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>Sept 11<sup>th</sup> [187]3.</p>
<p>Messrs P.O. Brien &amp; Co.</p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>
<p>As there seems to be some<span class='line-break'> </span>misunderstanding among other parties in regard<span class='line-break'> </span>to permits, I will respectfuly inform you in<span class='line-break'> </span>regard to your Permit (you have applied to the Trustees<span class='line-break'> </span>for) in order to prevent any inconvenience -</p>
<p>Your Gardening Permit does not cover grading<span class='line-break'> </span>sodding, curbing, tomb building, foundations, or<span class='line-break'> </span>any work not strictly gardening and I am directed<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Trustees to require a special permit for<span class='line-break'> </span>any lot upon which you do any work not gardening.</p>
<p>You may perhaps, understand the matter<span class='line-break'> </span>fully, but if not please provide yourself when<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary, with the permits &amp; send them with<span class='line-break'> </span>the sod, loam or other material you wish<span class='line-break'> </span>admitted with the cemetery and leave the<span class='line-break'> </span>permit with the Engineer.</p>

<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>

<p>In my note of<span class='line-break'> </span>Sept 15<sup>th</sup> in regard to "cleaning<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues," instead of 90<sup>cents</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>please read 91<sup>cents</sup> and adding<span class='line-break'> </span>10% please read $1.00 for 99<sup>cents</sup>,<span class='line-break'> </span>there being an error in addition<span class='line-break'> </span>which fortunately will not alter<span class='line-break'> </span>the result much.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132122">CB03_0309</a></h3>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='309'>309</span></p>
<p>Sept 15<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you below a few figures<span class='line-break'> </span>in regard to the cost of cleaning Avenues &amp;c.</p>
<p>(Estimate)</p>
<p>Cost of removing rubbish &amp; leaves every Spring<span class='line-break'> </span>$911.12 on 4240 lots, April 1873, say pr lot <span class='depth3' depth='3' title='21 1/2 cts'>21 1/2 cts</span></p>
<p>Cost of sweeping &amp; weeding Avenues thru the<span class='line-break'> </span>year $1336.50 of which one half should be<span class='line-break'> </span>charged to cleaning up after gardeners &amp;c.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>say</th> <th>$668.25</th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td/> <td>1747.20</td> <td>Cost of removing rubbish &amp; grass from Avenues (144 days as desired) </td> </tr> <tr><td> [total]</td> <td>$2415.45 </td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <span class='line-break'> </span>on 3500 lots (that being the number<span class='line-break'> </span>it is estimated that work is done on, which makes <span class='line-break'> </span>it necessary to remove any rubbish from Avenues)<span class='line-break'> </span>say pr lot <span class='depth3' depth='3' title='69 1/2 cts'>69 1/2 cts</span><span class='line-break'> </span>[total] <span class='depth3' depth='3' title='91 cts'>91 cts</span><span class='line-break'> </span>(&amp; adding 10% making <del>99</del> cts;) from which I estimate that $1.00<span class='line-break'> </span>pr permit is little enough when the difficulty of collection</p>
<p><u>see p.308</u><span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<p>is considered, as it would be an easy matter for<span class='line-break'> </span>any parties doing much work in the Cemetery<span class='line-break'> </span>to take care of an occasional lot without a permit,<span class='line-break'> </span>and I can see no way in which this could be<span class='line-break'> </span>avoided.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132124">CB03_0311</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='311'>311</span></p>
<p>Sept. 16 [187]3</p>
<p>Henderson Inches Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>40 Beacon St. Boston.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Your favor of 15th. inst.<span class='line-break'> </span>is recd, there an 1808 feet in your 4 Lots equal<span class='line-break'> </span>to 6 300 feet Lots, for which the regular price for<span class='line-break'> </span>Top Dressg. taken singly would be and has been<span class='line-break'> </span>for several years $24. or $4. for 300 ft. If your<span class='line-break'> </span>lots are all in one enclosure which was not no<span class='line-break'></span>ticed at the time the circular was sent we can<span class='line-break'> </span>afford to do the work at $1.00 per 100 feet<span class='line-break'> </span>or $18.; this is the lowest rate charged any<span class='line-break'></span>one, and if you have paid less in pre<span class='line-break'></span>vious years, I think it must have been<span class='line-break'> </span>through some mistake, as our prices<span class='line-break'> </span>are not higher than they have been<span class='line-break'> </span>for several years past and $14. will<span class='line-break'> </span>not cover the expense of doing the work<span class='line-break'> </span>well.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering, Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>J.E.C.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132136">CB03_0323</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='323'>323</span></p>
<p>Sept. 22<sup>nd</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>Messrs McDonald &amp; Sons</p>
<p>Dr Sirs</p>
<p>We shall be<span class='line-break'> </span>in want of some Mound Posts<span class='line-break'> </span>10" square &amp; octagon before long -</p>
<p>At what prices can you deliver<span class='line-break'> </span>as Mt Auburn as usual &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>when can you begin - By giving<span class='line-break'> </span>an early answer you will<span class='line-break'> </span>oblige</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132137">
<h3><a name="page-1132137">CB03_0324</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='324'>324</span></p>
<p>Sept 22 [187]3</p>
<p>N.G. Carnes Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The two lots referred to, in your<span class='line-break'> </span>letter of Aug 21<sup>st</sup> are lots no. 37 &amp; 290.</p>
<p>They are somewhat out of repair; the sod<span class='line-break'> </span>wants renewing &amp; enriching and the fences &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>sarcophagus needs painting which will cost<span class='line-break'> </span>for the two lots $100.</p>
<p>If you give me an order to do so, I can have<span class='line-break'> </span>your lots kept in order for you, expending such<span class='line-break'> </span>a sum as you may see fit to lay out, &amp; there<span class='line-break'> </span>will be no charge for looking after the lot except for<span class='line-break'> </span>the cost of repairs.</p>
<p>The corporation are prepared to contract with the<span class='line-break'> </span>proprietors of lots to keep them in <u>perpetual repair</u>,<span class='line-break'> </span>by the proprietors depositing a sum of money, the<span class='line-break'> </span>interest of which is estimated sufficient to cover<span class='line-break'> </span>the average annual expenses. I think 8 or $900 would<span class='line-break'> </span>be required by our trustees for the perpetual care<span class='line-break'> </span>of your lots.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132138">
<h3><a name="page-1132138">CB03_0325</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='325'>325</span></p>
<p>Sept 24</p>
<p>Miss Fay</p>
<p>Mr McDonald let'd me<span class='line-break'> </span>it will not be well to place<span class='line-break'> </span>the stones as you requested, as<span class='line-break'> </span>then will not be room to place<span class='line-break'> </span>all them at the foot of the graves</p>
<p>Perhaps therefore you will have<span class='line-break'> </span>them all placed at the heads<span class='line-break'> </span>of the graves, at A.B. &amp; C instead<span class='line-break'> </span>of the other end as you<span class='line-break'> </span>designated.</p>
<p>[diagram: placement of A,B,C in lot on Magnolia Ave]</p>
<p>Please let me hear &amp; <span class='line-break'> </span>oblige</p>
<p>Yrs respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Sept 24 [18]73</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Mr. A.J. Coolidge<span class='line-break'> </span>called yesterday to say that ifs he<span class='line-break'> </span>had heard nothing from the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees in regard to his applica<span class='line-break'></span>tion to place signs of "For Sale" &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>on lots, he <u>had</u> placed several<span class='line-break'> </span>in the lots, and notified the<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees of the matter.</p>
<p>If you wish me to take any<span class='line-break'> </span>step in the matter, will you<span class='line-break'> </span>please to notify me to that effect.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1132139">
<h3><a name="page-1132139">CB03_0326</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='326'>326</span></p>
<p>Sept 24 [187]3</p>
<p>C.H. Kingsley Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup>. Cambridge Water Board.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Our fountains are four in<span class='line-break'> </span>number and are run on an average 4 hours to 5<span class='line-break'> </span>per day. The openings are as follows,</p>
<p><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th/> <th/> <th/> <th/> <th>Areas.</th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Alice Fountain</td> <td>10 holes</td> <td>1/8 inch</td> <td>in diam.</td> <td>0.1227 sq in </td> </tr> <tr><td>Hazel Dell</td> <td>7 do [holes]</td> <td>1/8 do [inch]</td> <td>do [diam]</td> <td>.0859 [sq in] </td> </tr> <tr><td>Auburn Lake</td> <td>1 do [holes]</td> <td>13/16 do [inch]</td> <td>do [diam]</td> <td>.5185 [sq in] </td> </tr> <tr><td>Lawn</td> <td>1 do [holes]</td> <td>1/4 do [inch]</td> <td>do [diam]</td> <td>.0491 [sq in] </td> </tr> </tbody> </table> in the center and an opening an 1/8 of<span class='line-break'> </span>an inch wide around the circumference<span class='line-break'> </span>and equal to difference between the areas<span class='line-break'> </span>of circle having diamter of 2 inches and 1 3/4 <u>.7313</u></p>
<p>Total area of openings 1.5125 [sq in]</p>
<p>head is about 70 feet</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>[calculation in pencil: 3.1146<span class='line-break'> </span>- 2.4053 = .7363]<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1132140">CB03_0327</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='327'>327</span></p>
<p>Sept 25<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>S.C. [Clapleigh?] Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your<span class='line-break'> </span>valued favor of Sept 24 <sup>th</sup> and<span class='line-break'> </span>would say in regard to the price<span class='line-break'> </span>of a lot near the chapel, that<span class='line-break'> </span>we have but one piece on any<span class='line-break'> </span>of our lots offerred for sale.</p>
<p>I think $2<sup>56</sup> is no more than the <span class='line-break'> </span>land is worth and a lot near<span class='line-break'> </span>the Chapel has recently been<span class='line-break'> </span>sold for $3<sup>25</sup></p>
<p>I have several engagements on<span class='line-break'> </span>Saturday which will prevent my<span class='line-break'> </span>calling on you. I shall be at<span class='line-break'> </span>16 Pemberton Sq between 12 &amp; 2 o clock or<span class='line-break'> </span>shall be happy to see you here</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Sept. 25 [187]3</p>
<p>J.W. Grigg Agt</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Have you any covers<span class='line-break'> </span>3'6" &amp; 2'4" on hand? I want<span class='line-break'> </span>say 40 pieces if at same price pr <span class='line-break'> </span>foot, delivered as the last were.</p>
<p>If you have any please send<span class='line-break'> </span>us as above if you can deliver a <span class='line-break'> </span>part his week, if not please<span class='line-break'> </span>write me <u>when</u> you can &amp; I<span class='line-break'> </span>will let you know whether to fill<span class='line-break'> </span>the order.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='330'>330</span></p>
<p>Sept 26. [187]3</p>
<p>A.A. Barker Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The Board of<span class='line-break'> </span>Trustees at their last meeting<span class='line-break'> </span>voted to have all signs of<span class='line-break'> </span>"For Sale" &amp;c now on lots removed<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; to forbid that any be placed<span class='line-break'> </span>there in future</p>
<p>Please have any you may<span class='line-break'> </span>know of removed at once.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Sept 25 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr McArthur</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>At what price will<span class='line-break'> </span>you put up a picket fence 6<span class='line-break'> </span>ft high, pickets 1 inch apart, 4<span class='line-break'> </span>inches wide &amp; 1 1/4 inches thick<span class='line-break'> </span>to be of good stock &amp; well fastened.</p>
<p>Posts &amp;c to be good stock &amp; set in<span class='line-break'> </span>deep &amp; firm - pickets pointed at top</p>
<p>Please give me a price pr running<span class='line-break'> </span>foot for a ^<sup>picket</sup> fence 6' high, one 7 ft<span class='line-break'> </span>high, both <u>painted</u> &amp; <u>unpainted</u> for<span class='line-break'> </span>as much of the Stone Farm as we<span class='line-break'> </span>wish to enclose - Also cost of a board<span class='line-break'> </span>fence pr foot similar to that<span class='line-break'> </span>on Watriss Lot for same place- painted<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; unpainted. Probably 1500 or more ft</p>
<p>Yrs J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='332'>332</span></p>
<p>Sept. 26 [187]3</p>
<p>A.A. Barker Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have notified<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr. Ross to deliver us no<span class='line-break'> </span>more sods either of Couch Grass<span class='line-break'> </span>or Goose Grass. I want you to<span class='line-break'> </span>make the Foreman of the Sodding<span class='line-break'> </span>Gary understand that if bad<span class='line-break'> </span>sods are delivered he is not to<span class='line-break'> </span>use them, but to place them on<span class='line-break'> </span>the avenue &amp; <u>notify me.</u> I shall<span class='line-break'> </span>hold him personally responsible<span class='line-break'> </span>for using no sods which ought<span class='line-break'> </span>not to be used</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Sept 26. [187]3</p>
<p>Rob<sup>t</sup> Ross Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Do not deliver<span class='line-break'> </span>us any more sods with either<span class='line-break'> </span><u>Couch</u> or ^<sup>Goose</sup> Grass in them. They<span class='line-break'> </span>will not answer for us I am <span class='line-break'> </span>satisfied &amp; I have directed<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Barker to have no more put<span class='line-break'> </span>down.</p>
<p>I want a good pasture sod, if<span class='line-break'> </span>you can get it, if not, please<span class='line-break'> </span>see me before you deliver any<span class='line-break'> </span>more.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132147">CB03_0334</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='334'>334</span></p>
<p>Sept 26 [187]3</p>
<p>W<sup>m</sup> G.H. Smart Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor of the<span class='line-break'> </span>22<sup>nd</sup> inst in regard to setting a<span class='line-break'> </span>freestone monument. The base I <span class='line-break'> </span>learn is not here.</p>
<p>I can furnish you four men<span class='line-break'> </span>who are used to such work &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>a derrick, to work under your<span class='line-break'> </span>own direction at $15 if you<span class='line-break'> </span>take wish of damage. The die<span class='line-break'> </span>must be rolled part way I think<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; the derrick will lift it into<span class='line-break'> </span>place. Please give me a few<span class='line-break'> </span>days notice should you want<span class='line-break'> </span>our men</p>
<p>Respectfuly <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Sept 27 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr. S. Barker<span class='line-break'> </span>Newton</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>If the graves were<span class='line-break'> </span>mounded before, I suppose<span class='line-break'> </span>we should mound them now<span class='line-break'> </span>at our expense. It will<span class='line-break'> </span>be necessary for you to<span class='line-break'> </span>point out the position<span class='line-break'> </span>of the graves</p>
<p>Very Respty<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>by F.C.C.</p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1132148">
<h3><a name="page-1132148">CB03_0335</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='335'>335</span></p>
<p>Sept 27. [187]3</p>
<p>Alfred T. Turner Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Chairman Finance Committee</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The average cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>our plants this year has been 7 1/4 cents each;<span class='line-break'> </span>so that the total cost of raising 60000 plants<span class='line-break'> </span>is $4350, which is all we should pay taxes on if<span class='line-break'> </span>at all, as I have been unable to find any case<span class='line-break'> </span>in Cambridge where plants are taxed except<span class='line-break'> </span>our own.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W.Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<div id="page-1132150">
<h3><a name="page-1132150">CB03_0337</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p>Sept 29 [1873]</p>
<p>Messes A. Dow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you a sketch <span class='line-break'> </span>of your lot on a larger scale, which<span class='line-break'> </span>will answer to plan a curb by - <span class='line-break'> </span>Should you curb the lot, or merely<span class='line-break'> </span>grade &amp; sod it, I shall be glad<span class='line-break'> </span>to do any or all work required in<span class='line-break'> </span>a good &amp; substantial manner &amp; at<span class='line-break'> </span>reasonable rates. I have a large force<span class='line-break'> </span>of men employed by the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>to do such work for them &amp; for proprietors.</p>
<p>The curbstones we do not furnish, but<span class='line-break'> </span>all other necessary materials are constant<span class='line-break'></span>ly one hand.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Sept 29 [187]3</p>
<p>Ms J. Wayate</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>In purchasing<span class='line-break'> </span>the piece of land for a lot at<span class='line-break'> </span>junction of Thistle Path &amp; Mound<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues, you would have the<span class='line-break'> </span>right to erect a fence (approved<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Committee on Lots (of the Trustees))<span class='line-break'> </span>upon the <u>line</u> of the lot -</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<div id="page-1132153">
<h3><a name="page-1132153">CB03_0340</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='340'>340</span></p>
<p>Sept 30 [187]3</p>
<p>To the Committee on Interments</p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>I have applied the rule<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Committee, in the case of Trinity Church, but<span class='line-break'> </span>find no case where there would be any extra charge<span class='line-break'> </span>for records. There are 45 cases which at $5 gives $225 - <span class='line-break'> </span>These cases contain 116 bodies, but as a number are<span class='line-break'> </span>unknown, the work of recording is equal to 58 names at<span class='line-break'> </span>$1.00 say $58.</p>
<p>As the interments were made at the time the catacombs<span class='line-break'> </span>were building, there was no labor expended in opening<span class='line-break'> </span>or closing the graves, and as the cases were all received<span class='line-break'> </span>at six or possibly eight times, $30 would cover all cost<span class='line-break'> </span>to the corporation for attendance &amp;c.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<p>John T. Bradlee Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm. on Grounds.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>A picket fence 9 ft high<span class='line-break'> </span>can be erected on the Stone Farm at $1<sup>10</sup> pr running<span class='line-break'> </span>foot, and a 7 ft high fence for $1<sup>00</sup> pr foot.</p>
<p>Cedar posts [then?] rails let in &amp; spiked on which<span class='line-break'> </span>planed &amp; pointed pickets 7/8" thick &amp; 3" wide are nailed<span class='line-break'> </span>3" apart. Also a base board &amp; strip opposite top rail<span class='line-break'> </span>outside of pickets to stiffen them. All to be well<span class='line-break'> </span>fastened &amp; painted two coats.</p>
<p><u>Gravel</u><span class='line-break'> </span>can be bought of Alex. M<sup>c</sup>Donald for 20<sup>Â¢</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; perhaps 18<sup>Â¢</sup> a yard in [bulk?]. We shall want<span class='line-break'> </span>gravel for finishing Halcyon Lake, on Fountain Ave<span class='line-break'> </span>in rear of Receiving Tomb, and in the large hollow<span class='line-break'> </span>opposite Cambridge Cemetery, on both sides of stockade<span class='line-break'> </span>fence, as well as for ordinary repairs of Avenues<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; grading of new lots.</p>
<p>We can [trade?] &amp; deliver this at Halcyon Lake or<span class='line-break'> </span>the stockade fence for 50<sup>Â¢</sup> pr yard making a total<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of 70<sup>Â¢</sup> pr yard, or 10 cents a yard cheaper than<span class='line-break'> </span>I can buy it of any one I know of.</p>
<p>Please give this matter your attention, as con<span class='line-break'></span>siderable portions have been sold.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>Mrs Abel Tompkins:</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132166">CB03_0353</a></h3>

<p>Mt. Auburn <span class='line-break'> </span>Oct 10. 1873.</p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I send you the two plans<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Watriss and Chant Lot &amp; papers connected with<span class='line-break'> </span>them.</p>
<p>The continuation of the Northern branch of Elm Ave. into<span class='line-break'> </span>the Watriss Lot, does not meet the requirements I think<span class='line-break'> </span>All teams must in this case either pass the front gate<span class='line-break'> </span>or else pass around a sharp turn from the South branch <span class='line-break'> </span>of Elm Ave (near lot 3906) when they would be very liable<span class='line-break'> </span>to do damage.</p>
<p>The Southern branch of Elm Ave can be extended<span class='line-break'> </span>by the purchase or exchange of lot 2298 and this gives<span class='line-break'> </span>in my opinion the best means of access.</p>
<p>It would be possible to widen either Mistletoe Path or<span class='line-break'> </span>Spiraea, but only by the purchase of exchange of at least<span class='line-break'> </span>one lot. I think Spiraea path can be extended to advantage<span class='line-break'> </span>as a path.</p>
<p>On the southern side of St John's Lot, the path can be<span class='line-break'> </span>widened to 9 or 10 feet as indicated by the purple lines<span class='line-break'> </span>(present path in plain black) which would be wide<span class='line-break'> </span>enough for our own teams. It is possible to widen<span class='line-break'> </span>so as to make a very handsome entrance to the<span class='line-break'> </span>Chant Lot, by exchanging or purchasing Lots 1653, 2694, 2877 &amp; 3578</p>
<p>I have provided on the Western side for a large Public<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132167">
<h3><a name="page-1132167">CB03_0354</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='354'>354</span></p>
<p>Lot, which is I think much needed, the present Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>being too far from the gate. Two rows of graves are arranged<span class='line-break'> </span>with a path between. The usual border of six feet thus<span class='line-break'> </span>along the whole front of the lot, with an addition at<span class='line-break'> </span>the entrance, which I would propose as Ornamental<span class='line-break'> </span>Ground. The larger portion^<sup>to be planted</sup> with handsome trees &amp; shrubs<span class='line-break'> </span>and the borders sodded, with occasional flower beds.</p>
<p>This would give the whole lot an attractive<span class='line-break'> </span>appearance, as well as make it generally ornamental.<span class='line-break'> </span>Should this plan be adopted, would not some restricting<span class='line-break'> </span>as to fences &amp; monuments be advisable for the general<span class='line-break'> </span>effect?</p>
<p>The land is readily divisible into lots of 20'x20', 20'x15'<span class='line-break'> </span>15'x15' and 15'x10' which would I think answer any<span class='line-break'> </span>requirements as to size of lots.</p>
<p>The Western portion will require considerable filling,<span class='line-break'> </span>material for which can be obtained by sloping from<span class='line-break'> </span>the Eastern line of the Watriss Lot to Birch and Balsam<span class='line-break'> </span>Avenues and then sloping gently toward the S. West.</p>
<p>This grade will carry all surface water either<span class='line-break'> </span>toward the proposed pond on the Chant Lot or<span class='line-break'> </span>along the Watertown Branch R.R. to strike the stream<span class='line-break'> </span>which crosses M<sup>c</sup>Donalds Land &amp; flows back thru'<span class='line-break'> </span>the Cemetery to the River</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<p>Oct 22 [187]3</p>
<p>C.J. Morrile Esq</p>

<p>I have looked up the<span class='line-break'> </span>charge of $354 for brickwork on the Trinity<span class='line-break'> </span>Church Lot. The work was all dimension work,<span class='line-break'> </span>and required a considerable amount of care in<span class='line-break'> </span>laying, also the irregular bricks placed to hold<span class='line-break'> </span>the slate shelves added to the work. We ac<span class='line-break'></span>tually paid out, I find by talking with Col.<span class='line-break'> </span>Folsom then Sup<sup>t</sup>; $155 for 30 days work of a<span class='line-break'> </span>good brick layer hired in Boston, and the rates<span class='line-break'> </span>for 19 days bricklaying by one of our own men, &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>53 days labor tending the masons (which make up<span class='line-break'> </span>the balance of the charge) are certainly at reason<span class='line-break'> </span>able rates. I have the dates &amp; the number of men working<span class='line-break'> </span>each day if you want.</p>
<p>Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering.</p>

<p>I expect of course &amp; understand<span class='line-break'> </span>you propose to put in good stock<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; to complete it in a thorough<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; substantial manner.</p>

I will let you know<span class='line-break'> </span>as soon as the look is far enough<span class='line-break'> </span>advanced to put the pipe in</p>

<p>D. Wise Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find by referring to<span class='line-break'> </span>our books that your lot was sodded<span class='line-break'> </span>spring of 1871, and it seems<span class='line-break'> </span>to me as if my predecessor ought<span class='line-break'> </span>have made any slight repairs<span class='line-break'> </span>needed by the sod; still I feel<span class='line-break'> </span>ready to do what is fair &amp; will by &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>improve the condition somewhat.</p>
<p>I find we have an order to top dress<span class='line-break'> </span>at $4 from you, and the repairs &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>top dressing will I hope make a<span class='line-break'> </span>good sod.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>Sam<sup>l</sup>. Batchelder Jr.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have looked at<span class='line-break'> </span>lot #1204 as requested, and find we<span class='line-break'> </span>have an order for annual care<span class='line-break'> </span>only. The lot has been attended to<span class='line-break'> </span>as often as others during the summer,<span class='line-break'> </span>and is now in fair condition.</p>
<p>The trees shade the lot enough to<span class='line-break'> </span>hurt the sod somewhat, so that tho'<span class='line-break'> </span>it has been cut often enough it is<span class='line-break'> </span>only in fair order. The myrtle in<span class='line-break'> </span>the flower beds has only been saved<span class='line-break'> </span>by great care, &amp; I cannot see but<span class='line-break'> </span>what the look looks very well. Certainly<span class='line-break'> </span>our part has been done. I cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>find that any complaint has ever been<span class='line-break'> </span>made here.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Mr. Mackintosh sends me<span class='line-break'> </span>your bill &amp; also a note in regard to it.</p>
<p>After looking at it carefully, I can find no<span class='line-break'> </span>error. You gave me the order in May &amp; it was<span class='line-break'> </span>not executed correctly at first, but I had it<span class='line-break'> </span>altered &amp; supposed that you found it satisfactory.<span class='line-break'> </span>In the bill you paid on May 15<sup>th</sup> amounting to $96<sup>25</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>I do not find this work included, that amount<span class='line-break'> </span>being for work done for you under Col. <div id="page-1132195">
<h3><a name="page-1132195">CB03_0382</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='382'>382</span></p>
<p>Nov. 5<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>Joseph W. Pattersen Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor of the 3rd inst,<span class='line-break'> </span>and note what you say in regard to the finishing of the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot. I should agree with you that we ought to share<span class='line-break'> </span>in the expense of filling, were not the price low &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>fixed low on account of the excess of work in com<span class='line-break'></span>pleting over must of our lots. Lots on the avenue<span class='line-break'> </span>just below bring $2.50 pr foot, and it costs $125 to<span class='line-break'> </span>finish at <u>least</u>, making, a total of $1025 for a lot of<span class='line-break'> </span>the same size as you have purchased. I can <u>complete</u><span class='line-break'> </span>yours at $200. or less, which will only make your lot<span class='line-break'> </span>cost about $2.05 pr foot when finished. Hoping that<span class='line-break'> </span>this will meet your approval &amp; that you will authorize<span class='line-break'> </span>me to complete the lot</p>
<p>I am yours respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<p>I have your favor the 8<sup>th</sup> ints.<span class='line-break'> </span>The lots #851 &amp; 1896 were topdressed on <u>Nov. 5<sup>th</sup></u>;<span class='line-break'> </span>the charge on #1896 was not rendered at the time the<span class='line-break'> </span>rest were on account of an overcharge, since corrected,<span class='line-break'> </span>the orders have been <u>recorded</u>, however ever since the<span class='line-break'> </span>day received, and the lots were attended to among<span class='line-break'> </span>the first. We have so many small gardening charges to<span class='line-break'> </span>be entered on the Treasurer's books every fall, that<span class='line-break'> </span>occasionally a bill is rendered before some small<span class='line-break'> </span>part of the order is completed, but of course I don't<span class='line-break'> </span>ask or expect any one to pay until the work has been<span class='line-break'> </span>examined.</p>
<p>The last order you signed was for care for <u>1874</u>.<span class='line-break'> </span>We do not usually ask for orders so early, but it was<span class='line-break'> </span>found more convenient to do so this year. I regret<span class='line-break'> </span></p>

<h3><a name="page-1132204">CB03_0391</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='391'>391</span></p>
<p>NOT SENT</p>
<p>Nov. 10. [187]3</p>
<p>Moses A. Dow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor of Nov 7<sup>th</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>In regard to price for perpetual care, I can<span class='line-break'> </span>not tell exactly the price until I know how<span class='line-break'> </span>you propose to finish the lot. If I remember<span class='line-break'> </span>correctly you propose to curb it. The sum<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary to keep it in repair forever, would <span class='line-break'> </span>be a sum the interest of which would pay for<span class='line-break'> </span>the average annual expense, including replacing<span class='line-break'> </span>the monument &amp; curb when needed. As I do not<span class='line-break'> </span>know exactly how our propose to complete the<span class='line-break'> </span>lot, I can only give an approximate estimate &amp; in<span class='line-break'> </span>fact the price is <u>fixed</u> by the Board of Trustees.</p>
<p>I should estimate the necessary sum to keep monument<span class='line-break'> </span>curb, sod, plants &amp;c in complete order at about $800 or $850.<span class='line-break'> </span>(You can deposit any sum "in trust"<span class='line-break'> </span>with the corporation &amp; they will expense<span class='line-break'> </span>income)</p>
<p>Yours respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1132205">
<h3><a name="page-1132205">CB03_0392</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='392'>392</span></p>
<p>Nov. 10 [187]3</p>
<p>Moses A. Dow Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have your favor of the 7<sup>th</sup>. Our price<span class='line-break'> </span>for "perpetual care" with a <u>Guarantee</u> is finally fixed<span class='line-break'> </span>by the Trustees tho I can give you an idea of cost.</p>
<p>The sums must yield interest enough to cover the average<span class='line-break'> </span>annual expense of keeping the lot in repair, and also<span class='line-break'> </span>allow a sufficient accumulation to replate the<span class='line-break'> </span>monument or curb when they need it.</p>
<p>If you intent to curb, the sum necessary would I<span class='line-break'> </span>think be $800 or $850, &amp; when the lot is completed, if<span class='line-break'> </span>you wish I will submit a sketch of the lot to<span class='line-break'> </span>the Trustees who will fix the price exactly.</p>
<p>Whenever you curb is ready, I shall be glad to com<span class='line-break'></span>plete the lot for you at a reasonable price.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<div id="page-1132212">
<h3><a name="page-1132212">CB03_0399</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='399'>399</span></p>
<p>Nov. 12 [187]3</p>
<p>J.H. William Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I find the number<span class='line-break'> </span>can be taken off the gate without<span class='line-break'> </span>much trouble. The best way to<span class='line-break'> </span>fix the monuments will be to sink<span class='line-break'> </span>a panel in the marble to take out<span class='line-break'> </span>the present wrong number, and to<span class='line-break'> </span>cut the proper number in the base<span class='line-break'> </span>of monument. This can be done<span class='line-break'> </span>for from $3 to $5. If you wish me to<span class='line-break'> </span>fix it in this way please let me <span class='line-break'> </span>hear from you &amp; if not, let me<span class='line-break'> </span>know how you want it altered.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup></p>
<p>Nov 13. [187]3</p>
<p>W<sup>m</sup> Holmes Esq</p>

<p>Your favor of the<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] inst rec'd.</p>
<p>The charge for 1874 for <u>care</u> &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span><u>plants</u> will be the same as for 1873<span class='line-break'> </span>viz $5. &amp; top dressing will be<span class='line-break'> </span>$1.50 extra same as this year</p>
<p>I am sorry that your lot was<span class='line-break'> </span>not taken care of in a satisfactory<span class='line-break'> </span>manner. If you will drop me a <span class='line-break'> </span>line any time when you do not find<span class='line-break'> </span>me, it will be promptly attended to</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Sup<sup>t</sup></p>

<p>[?] Sparks<span class='line-break'> </span>owner of lot 3397 [?] a passage<span class='line-break'> </span>way of 3 ft. outside [?] curb on<span class='line-break'> </span>the sides &amp; in rear of [?] lot.</p>

<p>I have written her [?] I have<span class='line-break'> </span>laid her request before the committee<span class='line-break'> </span>on lots for their approval</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Mt Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Nov. 17. 1873.</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm on Lots</p>
<p>Dr Sir</p>
<p>I think by the<span class='line-break'> </span>following means if it meets your<span class='line-break'> </span>approval, more work might be<span class='line-break'> </span>kept in the hands of the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; also the "boundary marks &amp; grade<span class='line-break'> </span>of lots" would be more under control.<span class='line-break'> </span>viz "that the committee on Lots direct<span class='line-break'> </span>me to require of each purchaser of<span class='line-break'> </span>a lot in future, an order "to<span class='line-break'> </span><u>post, grade &amp; sod, &amp; cut numbers;"</u> or if<span class='line-break'> </span>[?] intends to curb the lot to <u>"set<span class='line-break'> </span>clamps, lead curb, &amp; grade &amp; sod</u> lot &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span><u>cut number</u>, if <u>not cut</u>."</p>
<p>By this means the annual care would<span class='line-break'> </span>come into our hands for a year &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>probably remain.</p>
<p>It can be applied to tomb lots if best.</p>
<p>Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt.</p>

<div id="page-1132221">
<h3><a name="page-1132221">CB03_0408</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='408'>408</span></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Nov. 18. 1873.</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm on Lots.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have recently found in<span class='line-break'> </span>several cases that when two proprietors had<span class='line-break'> </span>curbed their lots either in one enclosure or at any <span class='line-break'> </span>rate connected &amp; without passageway, the numbers<span class='line-break'> </span>have been exchanged, so that the lot on ground does<span class='line-break'> </span>not agree with either catalogue or map in <u>number</u>.</p>
<p>It seems very important to avoid mistakes that<span class='line-break'> </span>all lots should be numbered, but it is worse to<span class='line-break'> </span>have a wrong number than to be entirely without.</p>
<p>The lots 2178 &amp; 2179 also 3428 &amp; 3429 are instances<span class='line-break'> </span>of this sort, both are curbed, &amp; I should be glad to<span class='line-break'> </span>be instructed in there &amp; similar cases either to<span class='line-break'> </span>have the parties change their deeds or their numbers.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1132226">CB03_0413</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='413'>413</span></p>
<p>Nov 19 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr. Reuben S. Wade<span class='line-break'> </span>17 Pemberton Sq. Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>In answer to the note<span class='line-break'> </span>at the foot of the order which you<span class='line-break'> </span>returned unsigned I will state<span class='line-break'> </span>that parties in no way connected<span class='line-break'> </span>with the Corporation have been<span class='line-break'> </span>soliciting orders for gardening<span class='line-break'> </span>work to be done in 1874; to one<span class='line-break'> </span>of these you most likely gave your<span class='line-break'> </span>order, which you will probably<span class='line-break'> </span>wish to revoke, as their facilities<span class='line-break'> </span>for performing the work in a<span class='line-break'> </span>satisfactory manner are very meagre<span class='line-break'> </span>as compared with those of the Corporation</p>
<p>Very Respectfully <span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132227">
<h3><a name="page-1132227">CB03_0414</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='414'>414</span></p>
<p><u>JW Lovering</u></p>
<p>Nov 19 [187]3</p>
<p>J.H. Willard Esq.<span class='line-break'> </span>86 Bow St. Charlestown.</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>As my letter of the 12<sup>th</sup> inst<span class='line-break'> </span>has not been answered, on account I presume<span class='line-break'> </span>of its not reaching you I will repeat it<span class='line-break'> </span>to your present address.</p>
<p>"I find the number can be taken off<span class='line-break'> </span>the Gate without much trouble.</p>
<p>The best way to fix the monument will be<span class='line-break'> </span>to sink a panel in the marble to take<span class='line-break'> </span>out the present wrong number, and to cut<span class='line-break'> </span>the proper number in the base of monument.</p>
<p>This can be done for from $3. to $5. If <span class='line-break'> </span>you wish me to fix it in this way, please<span class='line-break'> </span>let me hear from you &amp; if not, then let<span class='line-break'> </span>me know how you want it altered</p>
<p>Yours Truly<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1132230">CB03_0417</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='417'>417</span></p>
<p>Nov 21<sup>st</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>H.H. Read Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of the 20<sup>th</sup> inst<span class='line-break'> </span>received.</p>
<p>It has not been <u>my</u> fault that<span class='line-break'> </span>you have had as yet no answer.<span class='line-break'> </span>I put the matter promptly before<span class='line-break'> </span>our Trustees &amp; several have visited<span class='line-break'> </span>the <u>spot</u>. I have been awaiting<span class='line-break'> </span>their vote making it ornamental<span class='line-break'> </span>Ground. I can inform you, however,<span class='line-break'> </span>with pleasure that those whom I have<span class='line-break'> </span>seen are favorably disposed. I<span class='line-break'> </span>will let you know as soon as this matter<span class='line-break'> </span>is settled.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering</p>
<p>Nov 22 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr. J.L. Batchelder<span class='line-break'> </span>356 Federal St<span class='line-break'> </span>Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>As nearly as I can<span class='line-break'> </span>judge the Tomb $3580 is worth<span class='line-break'> </span>about $4000. The four lower<span class='line-break'> </span>catacombs are worth $1000.00</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
</div>

<div id="page-1132237">
<h3><a name="page-1132237">CB03_0424</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='424'>424</span></p>
<p><u>JW Lovering</u></p>
<p>Dec 2 [187]3</p>
<p>Messrs G.H. Moseley &amp; Co</p>
<p>Gentlemen</p>
<p>I notice again a considerable<span class='line-break'> </span>discrepancy in the measurement of the manure, which<span class='line-break'> </span>I cannot account for; as our measurements agree<span class='line-break'> </span>with those of all other parties. Please send me <span class='line-break'> </span>the length, breadth and hight of the loads for the<span class='line-break'> </span>past month, which I will compare with our measurements<span class='line-break'> </span>and try and see where the trouble is.</p>
<p>I decline to recieve any more manure, measured<span class='line-break'> </span>by the present measurer without the length breadth and<span class='line-break'> </span>hight, of each load on the card, or else let it be<span class='line-break'> </span>measured by some other party.</p>
<p>I do not want any more until the<span class='line-break'> </span>Greenhouses are ready to use it, when I will<span class='line-break'> </span>notify you.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132238">
<h3><a name="page-1132238">CB03_0425</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='425'>425</span></p>
<p>Dec 3. [187]3</p>
<p>Miss Henshaw</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>I have carefuly<span class='line-break'> </span>examined the tomb you requested<span class='line-break'> </span>me to &amp; am of the opinion that<span class='line-break'> </span>no improvement can be made<span class='line-break'> </span>without rebuilding the whole<span class='line-break'> </span>interior of the tomb. This would<span class='line-break'> </span>involve a large outlay. I can<span class='line-break'> </span>explain the matter more fully, <u>if</u><span class='line-break'> </span>you visit at the office in Boston<span class='line-break'> </span>next Saturday.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Sup<sup>t</sup><span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1132239">
<h3><a name="page-1132239">CB03_0426</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='426'>426</span></p>
<p>Mt Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 3 1873.</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Lot #2370 Nichols was<span class='line-break'> </span>curbed by the Corporation Oct 20 [18]71. It would<span class='line-break'> </span>appear from the books that we hauled in &amp; set<span class='line-break'> </span>the curb. I do not know who furnished it, but<span class='line-break'> </span>as I find a small credit in the account for<span class='line-break'> </span>the old corner posts returned, I think the discrepancy<span class='line-break'> </span>would have been discussed at that time, if only<span class='line-break'> </span>180 ft were enclosed, instead of the 221 ft.</p>
<p>Lots 3777 &amp; 37778 need to have posting of the<span class='line-break'> </span>curb reset, clamped &amp; leaded at an estimated ex<span class='line-break'></span>pense of $30.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132240">
<h3><a name="page-1132240">CB03_0427</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='427'>427</span></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 4 [18]73</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Ch. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>On looking at<span class='line-break'> </span>Mr Sherburne's lots 3021 &amp; 3022<span class='line-break'> </span>I find that there would be no<span class='line-break'> </span>difficulty in making a passage<span class='line-break'> </span>way between the lots, and a<span class='line-break'> </span>strip wide enough to make the <span class='line-break'> </span>89 feet should, I think be taken<span class='line-break'> </span>from lot 3021, and an order given<span class='line-break'> </span>us by the owner to seat posts &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span><u>cut</u> the <u>numbers</u> (which has<span class='line-break'> </span>never been done)</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 4. 1873</p>
<p>John T. Bradlee Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Pres<sup>t</sup> &amp;c.</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>To take down the<span class='line-break'> </span>remaining portion of the fence on the<span class='line-break'> </span>Line of the Watriss &amp; Chant Lots &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>remove to line of Chant Lot &amp;<span class='line-break'> </span>Catholic Cemetery will cost $95<sup>45</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>and the remaining distance<span class='line-break'> </span>to line of stockade fence can be<span class='line-break'> </span>completed for $650.90</p>
<p>This allows for some waste on<span class='line-break'> </span>the fence removed &amp; is probably <span class='line-break'> </span>a liberal estimate.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<div id="page-1132249">
<h3><a name="page-1132249">CB03_0436</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='436'>436</span></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 53 1873.</p>
<p>Hon. Edward Lawrence</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Please find on the following<span class='line-break'> </span>page the annual cost of running the engine<span class='line-break'> </span>connected with our Fountains.</p>
<p>I tried the experiment of keeping no fireman<span class='line-break'> </span>in May, but as the Engineer keeps a general oversight<span class='line-break'> </span>at the East gate, I found he could not do the work<span class='line-break'> </span>alone. The Engineer's time from April 1<sup>st</sup> to Dec. 1<sup>st</sup> I<span class='line-break'> </span>charge in to cost of running the engine, but from Dec. 1<sup>st</sup> to<span class='line-break'> </span>April 1<sup>st</sup>, five months, I think his time should be charged<span class='line-break'> </span>to general expenese, as he acts as gatekeeper thru the year<span class='line-break'> </span>at the East Gate. It would be necessary, in fact even if <span class='line-break'> </span>the waterworks were removed, to keep a man in charge<span class='line-break'> </span>of that gate.</p>
<p>The cost of pumping seems high, but I think we could<span class='line-break'> </span>pump more water with a slight increase in expense.<span class='line-break'> </span>were it necessary.</p>
<p>Respectfuly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132250">
<h3><a name="page-1132250">CB03_0437</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='437'>437</span></p>
<p>Cost of Waterworks in Report 1873.<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>$1361.29 10% for interest &amp; repair &amp;c.</th> <th>$1136.13<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>Engineer's wages 7 months @ $70</td> <td>490.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Fireman [wages] 160 days @ $1<sup>75</sup></td> <td>280.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Coal 33 tons</td> <td>283.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>oil<sup>$12</sup> Waste <sup>$5.</sup> Fallow <sup>$2.50</sup></td> <td>19.50</td> </tr> <tr><td>Grate bars, glass gauge, &amp; cleaning brushes.</td> <td>11.40</td> </tr> <tr><td>Sundries, tools, &amp; kindlings</td> <td>42.00</td> </tr> <tr><td>Average annual expense</td> <td>$2262.03</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> From May 9<sup>th</sup> to Oct 31. it is estimated the<span class='line-break'> </span>fountains were run 150 days, using about<span class='line-break'> </span>one resevoir full pr. day,<span class='line-break'> </span><table class='tabular'><thead><span class='line-break'> </span><tr><th>Reservoir contains</th> <th>69.79 Gallons.<span class='line-break'> </span></th></tr></thead> <tbody> <tr><td>8" cylinder, 18" stroke, 40 strokes</td> <td/> </tr> <tr><td>No minute, double pump in 4 hours</td> <td>76,194 Gallons.</td> </tr> <tr><td>[Total water]</td> <td>145,913 [Gallons]</td> </tr> </tbody> </table> <u>72,856</u><span class='line-break'> </span>Average no of. Gallons pr day.<span class='line-break'> </span>72,856 Galls pr day for 150 days = 10,928,400 Gall[on]s<span class='line-break'> </span>at a cost of about 21 cents pr thousand gallons.</p>

<p>Mt. Auburn Dec. 8<sup>th</sup> [187]3.</p>
<p>Messrs Shedd &amp; Sawyer</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of Nov. 25<sup>th</sup> also new map. rec'd<span class='line-break'> </span>There are a few more lots (sold since your estimated the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of new plan) which I shall want put on &amp; which<span class='line-break'> </span>I will see you about.</p>
<p>The Stone Farm has been laid out, that is a plan<span class='line-break'> </span>has been definitely adopted. I think as we are to<span class='line-break'> </span>publish a new map, it is desirable to have the Avenues<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; paths located on it. To do this with accuracy, I<span class='line-break'> </span>suppose the sectional plans should be made with<span class='line-break'> </span>the paths &amp; avenues. and they should be staked<span class='line-break'> </span>out on the ground. The new plan was prepared from<span class='line-break'> </span>a contour plan made by Col. Folsom.</p>
<p>Please give me your advise on this matter - as to<span class='line-break'> </span>the best &amp; most economical way of arranging the work.<span class='line-break'> </span>You can probably borrow the new plan <del>from</del> ^<sup>at</sup> 16 Pemberton Sq<span class='line-break'> </span>Please make me an estimate of cost of putting the<span class='line-break'> </span>plan of Stone Farm on the new Map.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132257">CB03_0444</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='444'>444</span></p>
<p>Dec 9 [187]3</p>
<p>Mrs. N.B. Watson<span class='line-break'> </span>137 Cambridge St E.Cambridge</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>Your Letter of yesterday is at hand<span class='line-break'> </span>The price for the care of a Lot of 300 sq ft is 5<sup>00</sup> per an.<span class='line-break'> </span>I am not aware that any change has been made in the regular<span class='line-break'> </span>scale of prices. We have the orders signed by you for the care<span class='line-break'> </span>at this price and also for the expenditure of 4<sup>00</sup> for watering<span class='line-break'> </span>vases.</p>
<p>Our regular charge for watering a single vase is 1.50<span class='line-break'> </span>but when there^<sup>are</sup> several vases in the same Lot we can<span class='line-break'> </span>do the work a little cheaper as we did for you.<span class='line-break'> </span>Although in a dry season like last summer the cost<span class='line-break'> </span>is more than the amount we secure.</p>
<p>If you wish the vases watered during the season<span class='line-break'> </span>of 1874 please notify us to that effect, at the<span class='line-break'> </span>same price as in 1873.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132258">
<h3><a name="page-1132258">CB03_0445</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='445'>445</span></p>
<p>Dec 11 [187]3</p>
<p>Cha<sup>s</sup> R Green Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>P.O. Box 4502, New York City</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The high winds of a day<span class='line-break'> </span>or two since have blown down and<span class='line-break'> </span>broken in three parts the central one<span class='line-break'> </span>of the three Headstones in your Lot<span class='line-break'> </span>No 117 Beech Ave.</p>
<p>I judge that you would wish<span class='line-break'> </span>to be advised of the matter.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>JW Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
<p>Dec. 18<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>Mt. Auburn</p>
<p>Henry L. Hallet Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your favor of the <span class='line-break'> </span>8<sup>th</sup> inst with bill received which I regret<span class='line-break'> </span>is not satisfactory.</p>
<p>The charge no more than covers the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of time &amp; material to us, and<span class='line-break'> </span>was made as low as possible because<span class='line-break'> </span>you were disappointed by our mistake;<span class='line-break'> </span>and you are <u>not charged</u> for the time<span class='line-break'> </span>used in <u>correcting</u> the mistake.</p>
<p>I should not know where to begin,<span class='line-break'> </span>were I to make the charge any less,<span class='line-break'> </span>unless I cancelled it altogether.</p>
<p>I supposed when the work was<span class='line-break'> </span>finally done that it was satisfac<span class='line-break'></span>tory to you, if not, I will cancel<span class='line-break'> </span>the entire charge, if you cannot<span class='line-break'> </span>satisfy yourself that it is a just one, as<span class='line-break'> </span>I believe it to be.</p>
<p>Yrs truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1132259">CB03_0446</a></h3>

<p>Dec 13 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr Joseph Collins</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>On and after Jan. 1. 1874<span class='line-break'> </span>any agreement, as to price for<span class='line-break'> </span>any work made with Proprietors<span class='line-break'> </span>must be entered on the order in<span class='line-break'> </span>full, otherwise the work will be<span class='line-break'> </span>charged for, at <u>regular rates</u> and<span class='line-break'> </span><u>no abatement</u> will be made.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>

<div id="page-1132261">
<h3><a name="page-1132261">CB03_0448</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='448'>448</span></p>
<p>Dec. 15<sup>th</sup> [187]3.</p>
<p>E.F. Young Esq</p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>As soon as you can make time I<span class='line-break'> </span>wish you to take an account of all tools which<span class='line-break'> </span>can be found belonging to the Cemetery, and you<span class='line-break'> </span>are authorized to have all not in less taken to the<span class='line-break'> </span>tool shop.</p>
<p>Charge to each man the tools you leave in his possession<span class='line-break'> </span>making him understand that he will be held responsible<span class='line-break'> </span>for their return to you, whole or broken. I think you better<span class='line-break'> </span>provide yourself with the numbers &amp; brands to number each<span class='line-break'> </span>tool.</p>
<p>In issuing new tools charge to the individual, except<span class='line-break'> </span>that should Mr Collins, or Mr Barker find it necessary<span class='line-break'> </span>at any time to send for a number of tools, issue them<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; charge to them, until returned.</p>
<p>This rule to apply to tools furnished the Greenhouse, [Mr Foster?]<span class='line-break'> </span>the gate, barn &amp;c. and to be carried into effect at once.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />
<div id="page-1132262">
<h3><a name="page-1132262">CB03_0449</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='449'>449</span></p>
<p>Dec. 15<sup>th</sup> [187]3.</p>
<p>J. Collins Esq</p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>On &amp; after Jan. 1<sup>st</sup> 1874.<span class='line-break'> </span>in accordance with the regulation<span class='line-break'> </span>of the Board of Trustees that no<span class='line-break'> </span>materials or labor shall be furnished<span class='line-break'> </span>without a written order, you will<span class='line-break'> </span>please see that whoever attends<span class='line-break'> </span>to the sales at Greenhouse, takes<span class='line-break'> </span>an order for all plants or flowers<span class='line-break'> </span>not paid for at the time, and<span class='line-break'> </span>that these orders are returned to<span class='line-break'> </span>me. I wish that no bills should<span class='line-break'> </span>be made except by me.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering<span class='line-break'> </span>Supt.</p>
<p>Dec 16 [187]3</p>
<p>C R Green Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>P.O. Box 4502 New York City</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your letter of the 12 inst<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. We have obtained the<span class='line-break'> </span>estimates of two Stone workers, who<span class='line-break'> </span>give the following estimates viz:<span class='line-break'> </span>R. Sands of Mt. Auburn estimates the<span class='line-break'> </span>cost of a new stone to exactly replace<span class='line-break'> </span>the old one at $80.00 and the cost of<span class='line-break'> </span>redowelling the other two at $5.00 each.</p>
<p>Alex<sup>r</sup> McDonald same Post office, estimates<span class='line-break'> </span>the cost of a new stone @ $100.00 &amp; redowel<span class='line-break'></span>ling the others at $5.00 each in connection with<span class='line-break'> </span>the new stone or $8.00 each if the new stone<span class='line-break'> </span>is not put up. I would suggest that<span class='line-break'> </span>any further communications be addressed<span class='line-break'> </span>to either of these parties as the Corporation<span class='line-break'> </span>does no work of the kind.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully James W Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
<p>These parties also report, that it is impossible to mend the broken stone</p>
</div>
</div>

<h3><a name="page-1132265">CB03_0452</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='452'>452</span></p>
<p>Dec 17 [187]3</p>
<p>John K Deane<span class='line-break'> </span>Under Tremont House, Boston:</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>Your letter of the 15 inst - is<span class='line-break'> </span>received and in reply I would state that <u>no</u><span class='line-break'> </span>order was sent for your signature from the<span class='line-break'> </span>office of the Corporation, previous to the one refer<span class='line-break'></span>ed to in your letter.  We have <u>no</u> order on<span class='line-break'> </span>file for the care &amp;c of your lot during the<span class='line-break'> </span>year <u>1874</u>. There are two outside parties who do<span class='line-break'> </span>a little of the gardening work who have no<span class='line-break'> </span>connection whatever with the Corporation. It seems<span class='line-break'> </span>probable that not being aware of the fact you<span class='line-break'> </span>may have signed an order sent by them.<span class='line-break'> </span>Such being the case, if you return us the<span class='line-break'> </span>order signed, with such alterations and additions<span class='line-break'> </span>as you see fit to make we will endeavor to carry<span class='line-break'> </span>out your instructions in a satisfactory manner.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully       <span class='line-break'> </span>James W.Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
<p>The Lot was top dressed with the manure as you ordered by the Corporation this fall.<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>

<p>Dec. 18 [1873]</p>
<p>Mr. H.B. Mackintosh</p>

<p>On the List of Bills sent you<span class='line-break'> </span>Nov. 24, 1873 is one to Squire &amp; Gragg Lots 4247 &amp; 4248<span class='line-break'> </span>for Grading Sodding Setting Curb &amp;c. amounting to $202.<sup>61/100</sup><span class='line-break'> </span>rendered Thos. Hence at the request of the <span class='line-break'> </span>parties I have rendered to each a new bill viz<span class='line-break'> </span>#4247  Geo. H Squire Arlington $121.57<span class='line-break'> </span>4248 Mrs. Oliver Gragg $ 81.04. Mrs. Gragg paid<span class='line-break'> </span>the Gate Keeper this morning. Mr Squire will call<span class='line-break'> </span>at your office to pay his bill.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132268">CB03_0455</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='455'>455</span></p>
<p>Dec 19 [187]3</p>
<p>A.J. Wilkinson Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>31 Brattle St  Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>We have received an order for<span class='line-break'> </span>the care of Lots #927,&amp; #3500. for the<span class='line-break'> </span>year <u>1874</u>. There are one or two parties<span class='line-break'> </span>who have no connection with the<span class='line-break'> </span>Corporation, who are soliciting orders<span class='line-break'> </span>for work to be done during next<span class='line-break'> </span>year. Not being aware of the care<span class='line-break'> </span>you have probably unintentionally<span class='line-break'> </span>given them an order.  If you wish <span class='line-break'> </span>to recind the order given to those<span class='line-break'> </span>outside parties and to give us an<span class='line-break'> </span>order for the work we will<span class='line-break'> </span>endeavor to perform such work<span class='line-break'> </span>to your satisfaction. The orders<span class='line-break'> </span>for top dressing were received some<span class='line-break'> </span>time back &amp; the work finished</p>
<p>Very Resp'ly  <span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Dec 19 [187]3</p>
<p>Mrs. W<sup>m</sup>. B. Oliver<span class='line-break'> </span>Care Arthur Williams 13 Broad St Boston</p>
<p>Dear Madam</p>
<p>The myrtle has<span class='line-break'> </span>been covered as you desired.<span class='line-break'> </span>It is customary to protect the<span class='line-break'> </span>myrtle of those Lots of which we<span class='line-break'> </span>have charge free of extra cost.<span class='line-break'> </span>If you will favor us with<span class='line-break'> </span>an order for the care &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>of your lot for 1874 we<span class='line-break'> </span>will make no charge for the<span class='line-break'> </span>covering the myrtle, otherwise<span class='line-break'> </span>we will be obliged to charge<span class='line-break'> </span>you the regular price for<span class='line-break'> </span>the work, viz: $1.00</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132269">CB03_0456</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='456'>456</span></p>
<p>Dec 19<sup>th</sup> [187]3</p>
<p>S.T. Snow, Ch. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>D[ea]r Sir</p>
<p>Mr Sherburne's lot measured to inside<span class='line-break'> </span>of posts contains the correct quantity of land.</p>
<p>The lot is marked on the sectional plans here as<span class='line-break'> </span>measured to outside of posts, and it escaped notice<span class='line-break'> </span>that the discrepancy was just equal to the difference<span class='line-break'> </span>in measurements. Perhaps the whole trouble may have<span class='line-break'> </span>arisen from an error in sectional plans.</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>

<p>Dec 19 [187]3</p>

<p>Your note of the 18 inst.<span class='line-break'> </span>is at hand. I have no objection<span class='line-break'> </span>to your sending the posts along<span class='line-break'> </span>at your convenience and sending<span class='line-break'> </span>a bill for them in the spring,<span class='line-break'> </span><u>provided</u>, that you do not<span class='line-break'> </span>send more posts than I<span class='line-break'> </span>ordered from you some time<span class='line-break'> </span>since.</p>

<p>Dec 22 [187]3</p>
<p>A.J. Wilkinson Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>Your note of the 20 inst<span class='line-break'> </span>is received. As we cared for your<span class='line-break'> </span>Lot the last year for $5.00 we will<span class='line-break'> </span>do so this next year, rather than<span class='line-break'> </span>you should change.</p>
<p>The order you have previously given<span class='line-break'> </span>was probably to either Fox or P.<span class='line-break'> </span>O'Brien &amp; Co. If you see fit to<span class='line-break'> </span>send us an order we can inform<span class='line-break'> </span>the other parties of your wish<span class='line-break'> </span>that we should perform the<span class='line-break'> </span>work, which we will endeavor<span class='line-break'> </span>to make satisfactory to yourself.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132272">CB03_0459</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='459'>459</span></p>
<p>Dec 23 [187]3</p>
<p>Winthrop A. Ward Esq:<span class='line-break'> </span>Cambridgeport</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Yours of 22<sup>d</sup> received.<span class='line-break'> </span>You have not paid for the care &amp;c<span class='line-break'> </span>for 1872 at the office <u>here</u>. I have<span class='line-break'> </span>sent to the Treas. at Boston who<span class='line-break'> </span>will notify you if you have<span class='line-break'> </span>paid that bill there.</p>
<p>With this please find enclosed<span class='line-break'> </span>bill reciepted viz: 1873~$6.50</p>
<p>Yours truly<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
<p>Dec 23 [187]3</p>
<p>Mr HB Mackintosh Treas.</p>
<p>Dear Sir,</p>
<p>Please find with<span class='line-break'> </span>this a note &amp; Bill from W.A.<span class='line-break'> </span>Ward. On the Bill the ac/c for<span class='line-break'> </span>1873 viz: $6.50 has been paid<span class='line-break'> </span>the G.K. &amp; Mr Wards sends an<span class='line-break'> </span>explanation concerning the<span class='line-break'> </span>balance in the note.</p>
<p>Please inform^<sup>him</sup> whether or not<span class='line-break'> </span>he is right.</p>
<p>Very Respect'y<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs<span class='line-break'> </span></p>
</div>
</div>

<div id="page-1132273">
<h3><a name="page-1132273">CB03_0460</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='460'>460</span></p>
<p>Mt. Auburn<span class='line-break'> </span>Dec. 23. 1873.</p>
<p>S.T. Snow Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>Chair. Comm. on Lots</p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>I have seen Messrs Shedd<span class='line-break'> </span>&amp; Sawyer in regard to the surveys necessary to be<span class='line-break'> </span>made on the Stone Farm before the lithographic<span class='line-break'> </span>stone can be correctly altered.</p>
<p>The avenues should be staked on the ground. These<span class='line-break'> </span>stakes would serve to grade from, and will ensure a<span class='line-break'> </span>more correct map, beside reducing the amount of work<span class='line-break'> </span>necessary to place the new lots sold on sectional plans<span class='line-break'> </span>which I would only propose to make, as avenues or lots<span class='line-break'> </span>are <u>completed</u>.</p>
<p>To do this and to make the alterations on the new map<span class='line-break'> </span>for the lithographer will cost from $300 to $350.</p>
<p>Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>J.W. Lovering</p>
</div>
</div>
<br />

<h3><a name="page-1132274">CB03_0461</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='461'>461</span></p>
<p>Dec 24 [187]3</p>
<p>E.F. Young Esq</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>Please send<span class='line-break'> </span>to this office all the permits you<span class='line-break'> </span>have now. Also after the<span class='line-break'> </span>1<sup>st</sup> day of Jan 1874 Please return<span class='line-break'> </span>the permits to me as prompt<span class='line-break'></span>ly as possible. When you turn<span class='line-break'> </span>in the permit before all the<span class='line-break'> </span>material is delivered you can<span class='line-break'> </span>keep such record as is nec<span class='line-break'></span>essary, in a suitable book.</p>

<h3><a name="page-1132275">CB03_0462</a></h3>
<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='462'>462</span></p>
<p>Dec 24 [187]3</p>
<p>James H. Wyeth Esq Rep of Lot #1728^<sup>Carter</sup></p>
<p>Dear Sir</p>
<p>The Trustees have instructed me to<span class='line-break'> </span>have the Number placed on the lot, which has not<span class='line-break'> </span>been previously done; at an expense of $3.00</p>
<p>Should I do so, and deduct the same from the<span class='line-break'> </span>interest of the fund, the balance remaining would <span class='line-break'> </span>be insufficient to keep the lot in good order<span class='line-break'> </span>during next year.</p>
<p>Please inform me whether you would<span class='line-break'> </span>prefer to pay for cutting the number or to have<span class='line-break'> </span>the sum deducted from the interest.</p>
<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs ~</p>
</div>
</div>

<div class="page-content">
<p><span class='depth3' depth='3' title='464'>464</span></p>
<p>Dec 30 [187]3</p>
<p>E.F. Oliver Esq<span class='line-break'> </span>2 Bond St Boston</p>
<p>Dear Sir:</p>
<p>The myrtle has been<span class='line-break'> </span>covered as you desired in Lot 146 Central<span class='line-break'> </span>Ave. The usual charge for the work,<span class='line-break'> </span>where we do not have the annual<span class='line-break'> </span>care of the Lot, is $1.00.</p>
<p>Should you see fit to favor us<span class='line-break'> </span>with an order for the care of your<span class='line-break'> </span>lot for 1874 we would make<span class='line-break'> </span>no charge of this work, as it is<span class='line-break'> </span>customary to cover the myrtle on all<span class='line-break'> </span>those lots we have charge of free<span class='line-break'> </span>of extra ch'g.</p>
<p>Respectfully yours<span class='line-break'> </span>James W. Lovering Supt.<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs.</p>
<p>Dec 30 [187]3</p>
<p>Mrs Jane Hale</p>

<p>Very Respectfully<span class='line-break'> </span>James W Lovering Supt<span class='line-break'> </span>per Childs</p>
